Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», and it is that you do to the back of the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make three incisions on his forehead equally according to the length of his forehead; and one incision should be like two fingers wide in the middle of the forehead going down towards the nose, and the other two at the two temples above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries which are located at the two sides above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound should be the size of three fingers across together; and have a piece of sponge ready and lots of cloth without holes to dry the blood, then insert the sharp spatula which has this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; and scrape all the core that is between the two incisions to the entire surface that is above the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert into the first incision the instrument called 'scalpel', which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh near the heart, and the soft edge towards the bone, insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears of the heart, and then do likewise in the middle incision up to the other exit; and then extract blood equally, and press the place for the taken blood; then insert into each incision a tent made of old cotton, and cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil and egg white, and ensure that hot abscesses don't form there; on the third day untie the binding, and immerse it in warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The realm of eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has chronic catarrh with familiar symptoms, and you see their eyes droop and become small, their vision weakens, and their eyelids burn; the hair falls out, and on the head intense pain arises, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that this mucus and catarrh comes forth from multiple sources, and the moist membrane is affected, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And so instruct the patient to clear their forehead, then make a wide incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from ear to ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Beginning with the incision on the left temple to the right temple, let it be deep enough to reach the bone; avoid the nerves that move during eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe away all blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton and linen threads between the two lips of the wound; next bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, taking care to prevent hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, make a plaster of it; apply to these wounds to encourage flesh development throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The cleaning of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or beasts, or mine-stones such as iron; or seeds, such as oats, beans, peas; or fluids like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other object that does not fit or grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you can see the stone, drop a few drops of violet oil or oil of sisymbrium, then apply extraction; have them sneeze with force, and plug their nose when the sneeze comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and suspend the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Very often fire is used in this treatment; if fire cannot be applied, use the following method of extraction with fine pincers which is thus described:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it can be extracted with pincers, that is good; if not, use the following method of extraction with a fine sharp-pointed hook; and if this does not work, make a small iron rod and insert its tip firmly into the hole in the ear; block up around the rod with soft wax so no air can enter alongside the rod; then pull hard as fire is often used as we have said; and if it cannot be extracted by these means, use glue of which you will take an instrument that serves to catch birds, and place a piece into this; insert some cotton at one end; press the glue onto a stone or other such thing and extract with force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be healed by all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear rather than let an abscess form with heat and spasms; and the manner of the splitting is such that you should first bleed the patient with a cephalic vein incision, and remove blood according to its potency, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and cut a small slit in the root of the ear at the fatty place where it depends; let the slit be like a moon, so as to reach the stone, then remove it with your strength, and suck it swiftly into your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a swelling that has occurred and it inflates, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot exit, then use the slender spatula in this manner:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many incisions; then remove it with subtle pincers and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in the case of water falling into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing as a remedy, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If this should work, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many thin and light pebbles according to the length of your thumb, and warm them slightly over a fire; place these for the patient in the hole of their ear, and jump on it with their foot from the other side, pressing another pebble onto the one inside the ear; do not cease this pebble-by-pebble action until all the water is out, thus ensuring its total expulsion; if you wish, take a reed, and insert one end into the ear while holding the other end over fire until most of the reed burns away; then repeat with more reeds until all the water drains out, as we have said for stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	For the removal of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have mentioned in the division; but if it has a large body that can be felt, apply extraction with pincers; this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and discuss distillations, and the cure is not effective, then you must examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms appear, remove them with fine pincers; but if they do not show up, take a thread of this form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And thrust the most subtle tip into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck vigorously throughout the canal; do this often until all the wax comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey and come out, then pack the canal with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they still do not exit as we have mentioned, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proven for worm extraction, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, which is formed like so:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is made of silver or copper, narrow below with small holes and above with openings for distillation; and to press the distillation into the instrument, use a well-made copper tool designed for this purpose, and if you wish take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour in your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish from your supplies into the canal, and let the canal be inside the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand steadily so that the oil is distilled to the end of the ear; and the patient will feel it within, and keep the distillation only slightly warm when you distill it into the ear; and ensure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to the stuffing of a wound or something wedged inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes becomes complete within the ear so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes the object protrudes outside the hole, and can be clearly observed.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which becomes complete and cannot be seen requires urgent treatment in many situations, and for that which can be observed you must place the patient's ear in the sun; look inside: if you see an opaque appearance, treat with this entire remedy as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting at the front and back all around, so that it does not injure the ear; if the opacity is due to something lodged or embedded in the ear, then take subtle pincers and gently remove it until all of the object is extracted.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the earwax is completely blocking the ear, take a thin and light scraper, heat it slightly over a flame, then insert it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you detect wax causing the patient to experience itching upon examination, gently perforate it, taking care not to damage the ear nerves; then insert into the ear an absorbent material according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not remove it until the wound is fully healed; take a piece of absorbent material and moisten it with rose water, then dust it with ground vitriol; if you notice any swelling in the ear, you must first remove the old dressing and apply a new one moistened with ointment made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling subsides; treat as needed until it is fully healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and small cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and employ other treatments that stop the flow of blood as described in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper flesh
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This elder that comes in paper flesh from the eyes when they are moist and dry, should be removed with tweezers and pincers, and cut away with a spatule from its roots; then place ground vitriol on the affected area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is any remaining matter beneath, then use the subtle lenticular cautery; and after the incision, the cauterizer must be moved; and often repeat this process, as something may remain of its roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned away and will not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, on paper, there appear things that seem like hail in form and hardness, and this illness is called "grandine," an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; its treatment is as follows: watch if the grandine moves from one part to another, which is a simple thing to know; therefore make it wider, then peel each side lightly, take pincers and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot remove it without piercing the paper a little, this will cause no harm to the patient; and if the tear is large, bring it together with a suture, treating it until it is healed; and if small, make no effort as ointments restore it quickly and grow flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the cataract descends inside the ear towards the upper part, it overturns the eardrum, and one must grasp the cataract with forceps, and clip and press it from side to side; and if the eardrum is torn by incision, this does not harm; and once the cataract is clipped, wash the eye with salt water, and treat the place of what engenders flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat around the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinac is a fat that engenders in the earflaps of children and no one else, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because tears come quickly to their eyes; for this reason, they lie on their faces facing down, sleeping supine, and their earflaps under their eyebrows are moistened that the swelling and appearance has covered with exinac which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the bone between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The way of the operation is such that the patient places their head in your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a funnel-like device shaped like a circle according to the size required to contain the bone from each part, then place it on top; press with your fingers from one side to another so that the bone is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the center of the moisture using a sharp spatula, but do not make it any larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin perfectly until you reach the bone; and in many cases, the bone will come out of the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then entirely with a piece of cloth wadded between your two fingers outside, and turn your hand to the right and left so that it is spread out; be careful not to adjust into the fissure, lest you reach all the way to the spatula up to the eye, lest you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the splinter does not come out at first in the opening of the fissure, then increase the fissure slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten the cloths with oil and water, and place on the spot, and restrain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat [it] until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of an abscess with heat, treat [it] with soothing emollients until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs on papules.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papules appear with hairs growing in an unnatural way and they are inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause various ailments such as accustomed tears and softening of the papules and albuginea, leading to eye destruction; treatment occurs according to four methods: cauterization by fire, application of medicine depending on what was mentioned previously or described in the chapter on cauterization, done either by incision and suture or with canes, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand; if it does not comply, insert a needle with thread alongside the margin of the eyelid where the hairs emerge next to these lashes, and draw the thread above throughout the entire lid, and turn it over at the razor; then make an incision in the lower part of the eyelid under the eyelashes, cutting all along the width from the larger hinge down to the smaller one; remove the thread, and put beneath the lid a small tent of cotton and linen fabric, then sign above the lid with the shape of ivy leaves while still keeping to the quantity you wish to elevate the divided lid.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it so happens that you need to cut off a large amount of the lid in accordance with how much the eyelid is softened; then make an incision along its width over both lines that you have marked and begin from the larger hinge down to the smaller one, and let one of these slits be near the natural lashes like the thickness of a root, next insert the hook into one of the two angles of the heart, then remove all the skin; afterwards join up the two lips with a suture using a needle and thread made out of fine wool, wipe away the blood, and dry out any excess fibres from both eyebrows with anything that is sticky if you wish to do this; otherwise pay it no mind, simply leave the stitching and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches by applying drying and constricting substances, since the eyelid regains its shape when the wound heals and the eyelids come back together, but sutures cause inflammation (as ancient texts say), and these are procedures that need not be feared. There is also another way: one could sign above the lid with a figure in the form of ivy leaves as we have described previously, using three hooks separated according to this pattern:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut what is above with small scissors evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread and place it in the middle of the wound; insert one end of the thread near the large flap, and the other end near the small one, then gather the threads evenly between your two hands; lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin onto which you have stitched, as we have described; then join together the lips of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; sometimes, hairs grow from scabs: in this case, you must follow what has been said about incisions; but the suture on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is done in this manner: you must convert the paper and make a slit inside according to what I said, then make two cones by artifice, and also two fine ties as long as the paper and as wide as the width of your little finger; cut at both ends where you hold the threads; then assemble one with another carefully on that which rises above the paper of the eye, and stretch the two cones from the two parts formed; leave them thus for some days, and the skin which is stretched will die and blacken and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, cut it with force, then treat until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, remove the paper, and the hairs will no longer be able to grow; this is the form of the two cones that you will make according to this figure, and according to these quantities in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	li ovraiges est telz that you take a subtle needle, and place within it soft and delicate silk thread; then gather the heads and knot one to another delicately, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width long; then arrange in the shaft another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient place their head on your lap; and sit facing the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is subtle and delicate work, then push the needle through all of the shaft at the root of the hair close by, and make it pierce the paper swiftly until you draw it up onto the natural hair; then pull out the hair right up to the shaft, and insert into the shaft that same hair, whether there be one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come free of the shaft at the paper together with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the abscess is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the abscess from below along the entire length that you have ordered, until the abscess comes out of the orifice above and you see it by the sight of the eye; then you will treat the abscess and thread, and close the eye and let it remain closed for two or three days, until the hair dries in its place and flesh grows over; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair with them, and raise it up along with that which you leave, until they are elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the decay of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or decay, comes to the eye, there are two types of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or from a surgeon's knife, or from cauterization, and through similar means.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to proceed with this work is that you must split open said suture, separate its lips, and insert linen threads, binding it until it heals; and one should never use things that dry out or constrict in treating it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do not, the disease will return worse than before; but one should use softening things like fenugreek; and boil water or other liquid with flax seeds, then mix in softened diaqilon wax dissolved into any oil, wrap a thread in this mixture, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret to your cure lies in ensuring it does not heal following its previous form; and these treatments we have discussed are only preventative measures against this disease's recurrence according to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is dislocated and truly called 'axacrati', is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound, split and cauterization and similar things; the way to treat it is as follows: you take a needle with double thread on it, insert it into the flesh, pierce through from left tear duct up towards right tear duct so that both ends of the thread come out at two points in the eye's flesh; then stretch this flesh above all over the needle and cover it with 1 spatula width.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape on the paper returns according to what is required, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the split, turn over the paper, make two splits at its edges inside the paper; let both ends of those two splits be from corners of incision you made, and do so with angles such that when they're put together, their figure looks like the letter named 'I griesche'; then remove this flesh according to how much is hanging down below what follows after paper's edge, then join up both divided parts, sew them up with a thread of wool; then treat it with softening medicines and bandages until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a crack, suture or cauterization, you must make an incision full of folds underneath the hairs of the skin papers, and according to what is mentioned before; then separate between the two lips of a membrane, as I said; and one must carry out the work according to the form of the illness, because it has many diverse forms, and wise masters prepare all their power any kind of device in order to make the figure return to its natural form; and sick people themselves, according to what they need regarding work and instruments and various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the skin paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this fusion happens in men's hands in such a way that the skin paper is fused with the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, you must therefore insert the tip of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; stretch it with pincers until you cut off what is adhered to the fine spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt so that the patient does not suffer from the overly sharp spatula hurting the eye; make your incision in order to remove this assembly gently, so that the skin returns to its natural form; heal all of the aforementioned assembly, and sometimes saline is applied on the eye, as well as a poultice of warm water and salve; then place between the paper and the eye a linen membrane, and apply moist woolen cloth impregnated with egg white on top of the eye; after three days stop using the salve and any hot applications until it has healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the fingernail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You are a nervous one and similar to hard skin; and another that is not nervous, but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched by iron and assumed to be removed with pincers, cannot be; both types start near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all vision, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is as follows: have the patient put their head in your lap, then open their eyes for you; lift up the eyelid with your hand, then coil the claw-like nail around small pincers, and extend it upwards; then take a needle, and place within it a horsehair, or that of a cow or ox, along with strong thread; double over the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the claw, piercing all the way through with the needle, and tie up the claw with a thread and extend it upwards, then scrape away all the hair on the side of the claw where it meets the eyelid and the pupil right up to its head, then cut off the remainder at the root near the tear duct using a very fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh by the tear duct so that bodily fluid from tears may not flow through the incision; and sometimes the claw is extended only with an onion and thread, as we have said; then scrape it away with a very soft spatula of this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatule does not touch and rupture the fleshy membrane, and that the plum-stone is not pierced; afterward, pour into the eye a pinch of crushed silk, and from the litharge collar, leave it until the next day; then cure it with what is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the uncines cannot enter, this similar appearance of a nail is often cured by medicines; it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it cut, treat the patient's eye, and take a light sharp spatule according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not diminish and the root approaches, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar and crushed silk, and pack the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, like a warm abscess, then lance it, and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh in the eyelid harms the eye greatly, suspend it with a hook, and cut away a part but not all, so that no flow of tears comes; then distill into the eye red ointment made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh that grows on the cornea.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes there is sometimes born red flesh, which covers the cornea and rises above the sclera until it turns outward, resembling a rose petal; and thus they operate as follows: place his head on your lap, then open his eyes, and with suitable hooks remove all this flesh, holding it firmly; first cut away the top layer of flesh, then keep cutting with a razor right down to the end, being careful not to injure the eye in doing so; let the incisions be made with a spatulate blade as we said for an incision on the nail and with small forces which one removes the sebaceous matter, just like the diagram hereafter demonstrates; when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with ground seal or distill red ointment and similar corrosive medicines into it, then place over the eye cotton with egg white so that it is protected from a hot abscess; if nothing remains, and warm blood comes forth, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it has healed, and do likewise whenever such flesh appears in the eye by this procedure.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, you must ease the treatment of each weak eye by natural means and in case of accidental injury, with iron tools; and do not put your hand into any of these procedures until you see that this limb is ready for such treatment.
des voines des eulz	eyelid veins
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Beneath the eyelids are red veins that cover the eye, obstructing its function and weakening vision over time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary for you to first examine the eye itself in terms of where these veins are and whether there is another underlying condition apart from just the veins; then proceed as follows: instruct the patient to place their head into your care, and suspend those veins entirely according to your knowledge, making sure that the sutures be double-threaded following this pattern:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two ounces by degrees in I body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully coil the forces around those veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see the veins move away from the eye; be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, being very precise in your task so as not to cut into the veins; and once you have done this, instill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt that which remains from the tumor.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to gather all of this in that hour, make a plaster over the eye with things soothing to the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain subsides and the abscess has cooled, then begin again according to this method which is mentioned before until it is healed; and here is how you shape the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and burning medicine as I have previously mentioned, and it is not healed, there remains pus in it that you must cut open over the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove all the instrument of which this is made; it is called an "aspre chief" (rough head), and should be made of iron up to the head, pointed like a file as it appears in its current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers and press your hand a little until you know that corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the location with drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the wound is healed, and flesh has grown, and the bowels are also healed, and it remains so for forty days, and does not recur or become inflamed again, and no evil accident comes to pass, know that he is cured; if this is not the case, then there is another means of bringing about healing by making the fistula open into the navel according to this form: you must uncover the bone a second time with an iron instrument and appropriate medicines. When it has been uncovered, take one stick like this which has three angles at its end;
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place the stick over the bone near the socket and keep your hand one palm's length away from his eye. Then turn the stick until it pierces the bone so that the patient feels air pass through if he holds his hand over his navel; you can then restore the location with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens around the opening, the material will go to the navel; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens from everywhere in all directions, and there is no obstruction of the nerve nor diminution, you must bind the patient; then treat it, and apply cups or haterel without harming to suck out [blood], then put on the eye a poultice made of acacia juice, aloe, incense, and storax, then strain the eye, and place a plaster on top with bandages and soft cloths; and regarding the way of using the cloths, you should take some very soft cloth and double each one into four, then put one upon another according to the amount that the eye needs; then tie it firmly from above with a strong piece of bandage, and resume cups to suck out [blood] without harming; then remove the cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bindings become loose, you must tighten them strongly; then remove the binding after daytime and nighttime, and if you see that it is healing, this is good; otherwise repeat the poultice, the cloths, the binding, and the cups until it becomes healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of tearing of tough membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When ruptures occur in the tough membrane, it opens up and expels some material like resinous grains, which is dreadful to behold; if you see this happen, the procedure involves inserting a needle into the root of one part underneath until reaching the upper end, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the eyelid margin; pierce through with this, leaving the first needle in place according to its position; cut the thread at the double-threaded part and wrap a piece of membrane around it, tying it tightly; extract the needles and apply damp wool soaked in egg white over the eye; leave this until the threads dry up along with the membrane, then treat the eye with strengthening substances until the wound heals. In cases where the wound is constricted by the membrane on all sides via a circle of cloth, let it heal as such without further treatment.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great trouble, pierce them with a subtle spatula that comes from within the eye, and remove the white moisture and bring down the eyes, entering immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye's bowels
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, called 'alcunnati', is only the bowels of the eye that are gathered within it, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and to treat this illness, have the patient sit on a straight chair with the necessary equipment, then take their head between your two hands, moving it until you see the bowels coming above your eyes; then fix them there, and let the light descend and uncover, and let the patient see things as they used to; but if the bowels do not descend below, know that this is water, and should the descent of the bowels be arranged differently from what we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you seat the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision on the corneal membrane with one stroke along the continuation of the conjunctiva up to the cornea; when it is out, drip into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled together with honey, then treat with another remedy until it is cured.
des aigues de l’oil	Eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the similarities of eye waters in the dissection, and what is required to pierce them; we act according to health [or: medical science].
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light [or: sunlight], and tightly close the healthy eye; then place the paper of the [affected] eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-sided, or in your right hand if they are right-sided; then take into your right hand, if the eyes are left-sided, the instrument called an 'almagda', or into your left hand, if they are right-sided; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea with the thickness of a line in that white part of the eye at the level of the lower punctum, then push the 'almagda' virtuously and turn your hand so it pierces the white part of the eye until you feel the 'almagda' reach the empty space; the instrument must be exactly as long as the distance from the cornea to the end of the black part, which is the iris; then you will see the bone through that paper because of the transparency of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument up to where the water [or: aqueous humour] is, and press it under a way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the swelling subsides now, the patient sees it before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, and if the swelling rises again, put fire with the instrument, and when it is inserted but does not rise, extract the almagda lightly by turning your hand back and forth; then replace a small amount of powdered gem in the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye dressings or moist wool in rose oil and egg white, binding it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin with plenty of egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are some men with very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called 'alberit', of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Et so perce therefore the conjunctive solely, and do not go too deep, but make its place subtle, then pour in almond oil as we have said; and upon completion of this work equip for the patient an appealing darkroom, where he will sleep on his back at a place without light; be careful with all movements, take soft food, do not move your head to either side, and keep him tied according to its condition up until three days; then untie him in that same dark house, test his vision, show him some things, and then re-tie the bandage up until the seventh day; and make sure you do this neither during nor after incision treatment now, but rather ease it so that water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess is hot and comes close to the eye, then untie it before seven days have passed, and treat it with remedies for abscesses; when it has healed, then release his sight by removing any bandages and placing gold leaf on his face in order to cover this up over a day or two, and be so in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house step by step, and turn towards your affairs; and know that no disciple should interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iran who told us that in his country they make perforated alembics, from which water is extracted, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read about them in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of alembic forms so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be properly made from bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the top part of this should also be made from the same subtle material, while the bottom end is three-sided in shape.
de la char sor le neis	de the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or emerge flesh-adjoined things diverse, of which some appear as scorpions with many feet; and among these are those whose flesh is adorned with colorful fur, and others have soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For this soft and unadorned flesh, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and push those things into the flesh, pulling them out forcefully; then cut away what you can manage with a fine sharp spatula on one side until you know that all of that flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be cut away, open it entirely with delicate and light instruments so that nothing is left; and if you are not overwhelmed by the abscess, treat it as required; but for malignant abscesses, act quickly and cauterize until the blood is extinguished and all flesh is removed, then apply fresh lint and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose bleeds and moisture reaches the palate, know that it has healed; and if the moisture does not perforate properly, know there is cartilage on the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen a little thick, knotted at one end with a knot as big as an egg or smaller; and let the patient place the head of the nose over this thread until it reaches the brain, and pull by sniffing until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth; and children in school often do thus, and it is easy for those who want to do so; then hold one end which came out through the nose with one hand, and the other end which came out of the mouth with the other hand, and draw one after another carefully looking at the knots on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this so that you know that the worms have corrupted this flesh, then pull out the worm, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all remaining flesh; and then insert a bronze tube into the nose for some days until it is healed, and if necessary use drying medicines; and that is how to make an instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and its conductance is also the same; and if you see it, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have one handle to hold onto the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh above the nose.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often there arises on the head of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time, becoming quite visible; for this, you must cut it out at the beginning, and remove it all quickly, then apply a cautery or burning medicine to its place; if one waits too long to cut it while it is still small, take note if it is hard, of dark color, and without feeling: do not touch it with iron as this would be an abscess embedded deep within the flesh, for when such an abscess is cut, great malice can come upon the patient; but should this abscess feel soft to the touch, being neither dark colored nor deeply rooted, one may see it all cut away safely and without fear, then treat the wound with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when bone-joint treatments come to one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
