You must therefore avoid iron treatment, and for the one at the head you must also do so, and in that of an artery rupture you must make an incision through the skin lengthwise; then open the cut with a pair of scissors, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed; then insert beneath it a needle, and pierce it all the way to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you for the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then open the place between the two bindings with an introducer, until blood flows out which is inside, and let go of the abscess; then bring forward the treatment that causes growth, so that the bandages fall off; then treat this with ointment, as befits it, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to a vein incision, you must hold in your hand what you can of the abscess along with all the skin, then insert a needle beneath the place which you are holding by hand, and pierce it, and have a double thread there, so that you draw it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I said to you, binding one end of two threads in two parts into two knots; and if you doubt that the thread will come out, insert another needle entirely beneath all the abscess by way of the first needle's incision, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut away the abscess until superfluous things are removed from it, then remove the extra from the heart and leave what is bound; then put a cloth dampened with wine and oil on top, then treat him with tents and ointments until he heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Likewise abscesses occur in arteries and veins, abscesses form on nerves when they are injured or through excessive hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	They occur more frequently in shoulders and arms and all places where there are joints, and these are serious abscesses, and their colour resembles that of the body, and they are found in various locations without pain; and when pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not located on the surface of the body but beneath the heart; and it spreads everywhere, neither forward nor backward, nor below nor above, and one which is in a joint should not be cut with an iron instrument: perhaps contraction would result; and those that are on the head or forehead, make the skin ulcerous.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root; if it is large, suspend it using a hook, peel it off, remove it, and stitch the wound together, then treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging down.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	They occur sometimes in the belly and not elsewhere at all, this is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance, and it has subtle roots and large heads; there are small and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had fine roots, were slightly split, and moisture came out continuously.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found one weighing 18 ounces, and the other VI З., and for the operation of incision do as follows: observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelous is white and moist with a fine root; cut it open with a broad spatule, and apply the fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	In cutting there is often great loss of blood, and if you faint from it then cauterize quickly; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision with iron, use a well-made thread to bind the artelous as we have said, leaving it for two days; afterwards hold it tight and do not cease binding the thread until the artelous is cut open without trouble; and if the roots are large be careful when cutting especially near the belly but you can safely cut half of it then cauterize so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound, taking care not to cut the reddish colored thelul which has a poor texture and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess aggravated, and I will come to the treatment of cancer thereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when it breaks open at once.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the abscess comes about through cauterization of wounds or fissures in sores, and it is on the belly or some of its parts, as happens with other ruptures, or when blood flows from veins or arteries according to what was described before, or due to windiness; and if this is because of a rupture in the sore and an outbreak of the bowel, then the color of the abscess will be similar to that of flesh, it will be slight without pain, and visible through several openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an outbreak of the intestine, then it becomes more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers it will retract, but come back, or possibly it would be tightened, and greatly enlarged at the entrance of the bath after strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue, and it shows when you press it with your hand, as it does not constrict; but if it is because of blood, then these signs appear: abscesses that are large and hard, and punctured in varying quantities; and if it is due to windiness, it feels soft to the touch, so consider whether the appearance indicates arterial or venous bleeding, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You should leave the treatment alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For he has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance indicates an issue with the intestine or rectum, you must instruct the patient to hold their breath and lie flat and straight; then bleed around the abdomen entirely; then command him to remain in your hands often, then go around the place you marked before with a span; then extend half of the abscess above the whole large inch; then bind it with a strong thread or firm silk rope, and let the knot be on top; then operate on the extended half of the abscess atop the knot, inserting your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the knot, untie it and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the rectum, grasp it with your fingernail and cut off any excess; and if the artery or vein gives trouble, gently go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, inserting two thick threads through them, and thrust the two needles into what was pierced before in a cross shape; then drain the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you can see, remove the needles, leaving the place until it rots, and cut away dead flesh as it occurs; or treat it when it is soft and rotten, then treat the abscess as we have said; draw out blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place with what is needed, and close the abscess as described before; finally seal the place.
dou chancre	From chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken about the similarities of chancre in the division, and how it should be treated with medicine, and how one must avoid iron-based treatments; and we speak of chancre in an awkward place in the flesh, requiring great caution when treating, and the ancients say that when a chancre is in a location where it can be scraped out like a chancre on the breast, groin or similar areas, then it should be completely removed at its beginning; but when it grows large and old, one must not attempt to treat it for I have never been able to cure such an affliction nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, involves purging the patient with black bile at first; then make them bleed if they are bloated, and prepare the patient to lie comfortably for the procedure; then cut away your ounces of flesh or the chancre, removing all hair from around it, taking out all of the tissue without leaving anything behind; let blood flow freely until it stops on its own, and press the area well with your hand or something similar, and if the bleeding opposes you, cutting into an artery or a vein, cauterize until the bleeding is stopped, then treat them with another cure until they are healed.
de ydropisie	From dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously mentioned in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, as well as the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is achieved through medicine, and those that are cured by iron; so only these two similarities are written about; and one must not use iron for these II similarities: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because they are mortal things; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure is not beneficial, then consider if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as constipation and similar things; do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see that the patient is strong and healthy, and he only has dropsy and no other illness, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed like this: lift the patient upright with your hands, and have attendants press on his stomach by pushing the water to the lowest part of the belly, then take the spatumile spiny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And divide [it] into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	A point, yet not so deep that it can reach the intestine when you insert it, and cannot cause injury; then observe if the dropsy is connected to the intestines: if so, make an incision three fingers above the navel on the right side; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left of the navel three fingers down; and if caused by mucus, be on the right. It is not fitting for the patient to lie over the incision such that the superfluidity flows into this weak spot; then pierce through all skin with an instrument, push it in, lift your hand up against the whole spatumile between the skin and fascia like you would in flaying by a finger's width or so around; then pierce the fascia until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is where water gathers. Then pull it out and insert this instrument of which here is its form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is made of light brass or copper, and has on the bottom part one small hole; and on its side from one corner three holes; and two other parts, each with one hole; and the head is shaped like a feather, which corresponds to the form of the incision that scribes make when cutting feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the handle, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it descends onto the instrument immediately; empty half or a third part, because if you empty more than necessary at that moment, perhaps the patient may die due to the loss of their spirit from the wound, or they become lost, or they approach death; but empty according to his condition's strength and according to what his condition indicates along with his pulse; then draw out the instrument and hold back the water, and it is retained now for the heart which blocks the hole that I mentioned above, which you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from this, and drain a small quantity of water; do this every day, and be careful not to dry out more than just a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient's condition, and you leave a lot of water inside them, cure them with burial in hot sand or clay, and through profuse sweating or bathing and exposure to the sun, and deprive them of drink; cure him with drying medicines until he is dry, and cauterize over the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in their penis, or the opening is very small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It must be pierced as soon as possible with a very thin spatula, following this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a slender lead plug into the opening, and leave it there for three or four days; when he wants to urinate, remove the plugs so that he can pass urine, then replace them; but perhaps this is not necessary, as the urine which comes out will keep the plugs open.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the orifice is small then this (i.e., the lead plug) has been medicated as we have said; it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the orifice in its place are deformed, for no one is born with an orifice at the top of the penis so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis upwards; nor can they ejaculate because the substance cannot reach the urethra; this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient often lies on their back, then extend the head of the penis and the scrotum like the size of a feather, so that the opening closes in the middle as it should; and be careful of the discharge of blood which often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with what stops bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Pimples on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathe comes to the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle needle, and cut and clean them all, then apply moist cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the cancer is malignant, of a foul colour and stinking, you must treat it with cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cauterized it, and if the cancer is on a limb, and has penetrated partly into the flesh and partly outside, you must remove the cancer that is inside first; and when it is healed, treat what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the head of the limb is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption occur within the limb and in the flesh; so you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then bind with a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind and fig bark, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries aid in two conditions together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a lead pipe into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin at the tip of the penis becomes dry due to those who have not been circumcised, or due to wounds or abscesses, then you must peel off the skin with an instrument that is sharp enough so that the ligaments are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a serious matter to determine whether it is caused by a wound or an abscess, then you must peel it with a spatula on some part of the tip of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate between them, and place a thin piece of damp linen cloth in cold water so that it does not dry again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a breaking of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work willingly, especially on children, it is necessary that we do our best work and the lightest touch for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, for it was not used in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For the majority of masters and elders who performed circumcisions would do so around the age of one, using forceps and an entire lancet; thus avoiding the heart as it has two veins, and perhaps cutting the one above and leaving the one below intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and is the pain doubled; and in the cleaning which comes from the point of the limb, it is not secure; and in the cleaning of the nail maybe the iron escapes, and they run away, and often so arises that there is no need of cleaning and I want this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with threads, I have found goodness in this experiment, for the threads cut as cleanly above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut evenly in all directions with equal tension; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin, and make sure the first action is to make the child think that you are only tying a thread around their penis, and then you can move them however you wish; then have them stand between your legs, out of sight of any instruments or threads; then put your hand over their genitals and blow on the heart, pulling it upwards until the head of the penis is visible; clean away all debris, then tie a place marker with double thread at the base, securing this below another loop; hold them by the second band between thumb and index finger, cutting through both threads in one motion, then lift up the glans and draw out the head of the penis; allow blood to drip freely for some time, as it is good for you; apply powder over the wound, followed by a cloth covered with egg-white glue, tempered with rose water, mixed with red oil ointment that is good and fresh, then leave this on until the next day, healing them with other remedies until they are healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forceps for cleansing is as follows: the two blades should be curved and sharp, and the blades should be as large as the handle evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of cleansing is when the core inside escapes the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, rather than letting the flesh form an abscess; cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then use pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and that which is below the rod is swollen, let it be until the hot abscess is calmed, and lightly scrape it; cut it as you can, and take care not to damage the part of the rod, for it will cause no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things adjoining wound with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if it breaks out from the heart excessively, and goes beyond, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	treatment of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by obstruction due to stone, or frozen blood, or a bowel, or newborn child, or similar things, as we have said in the classification; and if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained because of a stone which is in the neck or opening of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over their knees; their feet should be placed on their back, and their belly extended from the upper part towards the back, and the patient's anus restrained as much as possible; thus the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone above, whereby the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument which is called a 'syringe', of which this is its form: made of thin silver, light as bird's feathers; its nozzle being one palm in length and half, and finely pointed at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, and tie a doubled thread to the head of a small bag of wool or cotton; boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; insert the head of the thread into the syringe; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, then cut off the excess wool and push it until it reaches the tip of the syringe, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, next anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg-white; et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, make the patient sit on a seat, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, gently insert the syringe into the penis, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, until it reaches the base of the penis, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; then bend the penis upwards towards his belly; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, advance the syringe forward up to the bladder, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, and have him feel it until he voids his urine, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; but if this is not done in the prescribed order because what guides it is twisted, puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, then stretch out the thread with all the small bag of wool stretched too, et li urine en suit la laine, and his urine will follow the wool, puis l’estrai fuer, then extract it gently, et fai corre l’urine; make his urine flow, et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, and restart with the syringe until his bladder is empty, et soit aligiez li malaides. and may he be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scalds or blood enter the bladder, and putrefaction gathers there, if you wish to distill water and medicine into it, use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three apertures: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see. The nozzle through which the medicine flows should be shaped so that it stops up the penis without any addition; then a small quantity of liquid can be withdrawn from it by suction when required. When you wish to instill medicines into the bladder, immerse the end of the nostril in water and draw on the other side until you have drawn enough water through the instrument; then insert the nozzle again strongly so that air does not get in. The liquid will thus enter and reach the bladder at once, which the patient will feel; this is the form of the subtle clyster with which we can enema the bladder: it looks like this
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or copper, and the head is higher up; below at the level of the chest where the cords fall; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you want to use for an enema, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a good double thread, and warm this moisture in a pot over the fire; next insert the head of the enema into the anus, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture comes out suitably, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make it circular, pierce it round about; insert a strong thread through these holes, put together the circle like one would sew a purse, fill this with what you wish of oil or moisture or water, and tie it to the instrument; act as if you had made a bladder, pressing by hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken about the types of stones and their treatments in the division, along with medicines; I have explained the distinction between kidney stones and bladder stones, all signs, and which stones require surgery; as well as those in the bladder and urethra; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones which form in the bladder occur more frequently in children, and this is a sign that urine escapes from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears as sand, causing the patient's penis to itch, and they may urinate often, then become constipated; and many of these cases cause inflammation of the anus; and healing is easier for children up to four years old, while it is a grave matter in the elderly, and average for those in between; and treatment is more straightforward for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes it hinders the removal of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, lift them up and move from underneath so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out of its place; then have him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands placed below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards; afterwards search for the stone and feel inside; if you sense the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the first touch, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is an infant, or your middle finger if the patient is a young adult; and push it into their anus, search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it towards the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your finger, and push it out at the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which has this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Make an incision between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the scrotum; it should be straight above the stone, and both your thumbs must be next to or near the anus, and the incision across should be such that it appears wide from outside, while inside it remains narrow, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will push out what is in the anus without any effort; know that there are some stones with angles and edges: they are easy to extract; and those which are underneath, resembling a nut, round in shape, with a slight opening.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must take care of it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine returns through an opening that the flesh cannot close; yet try your best to extract it, either by pulling or scooping with forceps, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have finished your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, then bind it tightly, and place a damp cloth on top soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then settle the patient back onto their neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, thoroughly wash the place with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of daffodil and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess becomes hot and causes corrosion in the wound, or blood coagulates in the bladder, blocking urine flow, which is known to happen as a result of this: press your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will infect the bladder, and rot it; then clean the wound with water, egg whites, and silk, and treat him in all ways you know until it heals; and ensure every time you treat him, you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicine to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and lodged in the urethra, preventing urine passage, you may excuse cutting it out by this treatment: perform multiple incisions as I say so that he urinates.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	If you forge an iron tool according to this form, let it have three sharp edges like a spike:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move backward into the bladder; then insert the tool gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; turn the tool in your hand within the stone back and forth, until you can pierce through to the other side; urine will come immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks quickly and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed; but if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above it, then slit the penis where the stone is between the two threads, extract it with the tool, untie the thread, and clean the clotted blood from the wound; treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	From a woman's stone.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Soon a stone may be found in women, and if it happens occasionally, the treatment is difficult due to three reasons: one being that perhaps the woman is a virgin; secondly, one cannot find a skilled woman who would expose herself to inspection, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third reason is that one may not be able to find an expert woman in this field; and the fourth reason is that a woman's stone lies deeper than that of a man, hence requiring a deeper incision which is feared greatly. And if necessity arises for such, then you must seek out a knowledgeable midwife, and since it is hard to find one, or perhaps there isn't any chaste and subtle inspector available; present the case to an experienced wise woman in women's affairs, or a woman who knows some of this art, and instruct her to do as you command regarding the examination for the stone; and look closely if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the vagina and search for the stone; and if found, force it downwards under her finger, and advise her to place her finger where the patient has pain, and press firmly with her left hand upon the bladder region.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	S'elle la trueve, si covient qu'elle la mueve de greit en greit des l'entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu'elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the symptoms, then you will understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if blood defeats you, place some ground vitriol where needed and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work so that the stone is pushed out, having with you the tools I mentioned previously when extracting a kidney stone from men in order to aid you during your task; if the blood defeats you again and this is due to damage of an artery, place powder on the wound along with tenting cloths and strips of fabric, do not start over or pull at the kidney stone as it may kill the patient; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed down, and healing takes place, return to your work until the kidney stone comes out.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramus is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white puss, which is beneath the heart of cows, contained within the egg; and it is called "puss", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, such that one might think it to be another egg; and this has no name.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramus is due to weakness that comes from cows, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on cows, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a shade tending towards yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and these happen more; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is in the white puss we have said, then the abscesses are rounded, rather long like the shape of an egg, and it does not open the cows, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the surrounding tissue, the abscess swells along with part of the egg-like formation, and so one might think it is another egg; but if the moisture is between the skin and the subcutaneous fat, it can be felt well enough; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try this test that shows its form as described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows this test, judge by what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to their condition and the fullness of their body; then lay them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and place a lot of cloth underneath them; then sit on their left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod towards one of the two sides of the heart in the loins; then take the lead spatula, and cut through the skin over the loins along the length down to the elbow, making a straight incision while removing the skin up to the white subcutaneous tissue, carefully scraping according to your skill; then pierce this with a water-filled tube at one large opening, and extract all the water, then place your hands, and extend the white part upward; do not touch the heart of the loins, only the white part; cut it all away in pieces especially its thin side, for if you do not cut it carefully enough, water will return; and if the egg-like formation should pop out during your work, replace it where it was once you have finished working on the white part; then bring the two edges of the heart of the loins together with a suture, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another disease, then you must bind the vessels that are suspended, fearing blood loss; then cut away all the surrounding tissue, extract the testicle, and treat it as we have described.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two roots; so cut away the other part as you did with the first one evenly, then wipe off the blood, and place on the wound wet linen soaked in rose oil; put over another piece of woolen cloth moistened in wine and oil, and cover both testicles, then put doubled cloths over them, and bind it all above with a bandage that is shaped like this:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two pieces of cloth, and fill them with woolen stuffing shaped like this and sew them together at the waist of the pants; one piece covers the base up to the back, while the other reaches from the groin area down; another pair goes over both shoulders, and all these are fastened in the belt loop; sometimes, this root is treated not by iron knife but with cauterization, which you do like so: take a thin lancet-like cautery tool, cut open the skin of the testicles as we described earlier, then heat it up according to what has been said before, until the white substance that contains water is exposed; now use this cautery shaped like thus, and pierce through that white substance in an onion-like manner, then scrape away the flesh with this sharp hot cautery tool:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And strike it in all ways that you can, so that you crush everything; and make sure the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be mindful of blood loss, and treat it like surgical procedures; and if anything opposes you, or an abscess becomes hot or there is blood loss or something else, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then administer perforation as I have told you; when you are certain through the signs we have mentioned that watery matter is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; pierce the abscess in the part beneath at any place across the entire width of the spine; let the openings be wide so all the fluid flows out; then apply cotton to the spot and bind it up; leave it for the rest of the water to drain away, then treat until the wound is healed. If the white cloth does not allow the water to escape at the mouth of the wound, you must insert a feather or an instrument used for draining water from dropsy patients such as that described above, and enlarge the wound; know that the fluid will return, and it assembles again after six months or thereabouts, when it is assembled like before, then let the patient pass his days in this way.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this subject there is fear in many situations, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say, therefore, that many abscesses come from the body, especially in the testicles; and this is a common occurrence.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known to be caused by excess bile and acid, which spreads to the testicles, or due to impact; and the colour of the abscess matches the body's colour; it does not cause pain, and is a severe abscess; sometimes these are serious, hard, and stony, with an intense color, and can arise from arterial blood or swelling in the veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When this is due to an arterial issue, it is recognized by the hot, tender abscess-like swelling when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who is suffering from a swelling of the vein is recognized by its tender feeling upon touch, and you can easily perform the operation on this likeness, and on other flesh; and it is that you cut out the heart of the tumors, then burst the egg upwards, and draw forth the white matter, and release the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hardened with its flesh grown together, then you must draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is aerated on the surface or inside vessels, you must release all that tense matter and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is behind, you must cut it all away, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is completed, fill the wound with wet wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of abscesses on buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a poultice similar to barley gruel, with the softening of the buttocks, and the patient becomes very ill when they defecate; and the cure for this disease is just as fearsome as the one before, yet we will tell you the procedure according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the scrotum suspension around his hips with your two hands, holding all vessels that are near to the penis and stretching them firmly; next, cut transversely across these vessels with a wide-bladed spatula until they are exposed, then peel back the skin on each side as we have described for extracting arteries in the temples; insert a needle there where you have double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein is revealed, then secure again to the other end; cut them directly in half according to the length of the body and remove the corrupted parts; treat the wound like others that require stitching such that no vessel seeps fluid into one of the testicles; for by this there comes about no harm whatsoever, but if venom has invaded all vessels then it is necessary to draw the testicles from every vessel so as not to deprive the organ of its nourishment on account of cutting these vessels and drying them out rendering itself incapable of helping.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the cheekbone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this branch is due to the section that affects the cheekbone or the extension on the abdomen in the region of the intestines, which causes them to descend from this fracture towards one of the testicles; and this fracture occurs either in the cheekbone itself or in its extension, and it comes about through these two types of excessive force: from percussion, jumping, lifting a heavy load, or similar actions; and when it is caused by an extension of the cheekbone, there are signs that it happens gradually over a long period of time, rather than suddenly; and abscesses form equally around the fracture because the cheekbone presses against the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are that when it is caused by a section of the cheekbone, it leads to sudden pain at first, and abscesses appear in various places under the skin close to the surface, which is due to the intestine protruding from behind the cheekbone.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the muscles descend with the intestine, getting stuck there and causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, it is necessary to escape from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is such that you instruct the patient to retract the intestine with their own hand into the wound if they can reach it; then have them lie on their back between your hands, lift their thighs; extend the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert the forceps into the navel as much as you need in order to open the wound, ensuring that the opening is such that the intestine may pass through it; then remove the skin on top of the white membrane underneath the skin of the testicle, between the second membrane and what lies behind the testicle; with your right hand inside the testicles' heart, stretch the white membrane upwards using your left hand, and lift the testicle along all its membranes towards the navel; instruct the assistant to extend the testicle upwards and undo whatever is hindering it from behind; search with your fingers for any piece of intestine entangled in the white membrane, and if you find anything untangle it, pushing it back into the belly; then take a needle threaded with four threads made up of ten individual filaments, insert it through the posterior part of the membrane, beyond the scrotum's skin, behind the navel, pierce the testicle's roots appearing from the filaments until there are four filaments; gather them together in cross form and bind the membrane we said was underneath the scrotal skin with a strong two-fold ligature; wind the threads around the filaments and tie them firmly in two parts so that none of the vessels which feed it can enter through, to prevent an abscess forming; finally, place another ligature following the first one lengthwise for two fingers' width and then on all other places according to the testicle's roundness; cut into the part underneath the scrotum's skin until blood and urine flow out as we said before; then apply oiled woolen padding onto the wound and bind with the ligature we mentioned.
