Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes, the white surface is cauterized as we mentioned earlier, after incision, due to fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligament until it tears by itself; and if it delays in falling, let it be washed with warm water, and apply what we have mentioned earlier, until it tears; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it heals perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernia cruris.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron instruments.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is treated like the branch which has a worm inside, in such a way that you cut the vessels, after the size above slightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of what is affected, until the vessels fall out; and heal it as we have mentioned earlier, until it heals.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Any time a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the tissue opens up; but none of the intestines descend into the cavity, and if they do, it is little, and heals every hour; even so, if it remains too long at this stage, then the wound or fistula grows, such that the intestine descends; and this happens because of the extension of the fistula which is in the groin, as we have said, for it becomes extended, then softened and swollen tissue opens up; and treatment can be by cauterization, as we have previously mentioned; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner: the patient lies prone on their back between your hands, then cut away the swollen skin of the rupture according to how large it is, about three fingers wide; and then remove the fistula which is beneath the skin that covers it, then take a rod and place it over the visible part of the fistula; and press the other end against the abdomen, then cut both sides of the fistula along the axis of the rod, and stitch them together; then extract the rod, but do not cut away any part of the fistula nor stretch anything or make an egg-shaped extension, as I have explained in the treatment for enterorrhaphy; then treat it according to wound healing.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the boys' hair, clean it up and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The knife is forced in without breaking the surface, and cauterization is better suited here for healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the skin of the calves
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of calves is softened in certain people because the bones inside are softened and it can be seen; and when you want to treat it, make the patient lie on their back, and cut away the softened skin over the natural skin; then join the two lips together with a suture, and if you wish, sew the superfluous part of the softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the sutures, and treat like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	Chastisement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisements are forbidden in our law, and for this reason, it would please me not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary except for two manners: one being that the doctor should know how to respond when asked about it, and know its cure; and the other, because we often need to chastise certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cows, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastisements occur in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, have the animal sit in warm water until its muscles are relaxed and soft; then grab them with your hand until they are reset and you no longer feel any dislocation.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: You must hold the animal down, and press its scrotum with your left hand, then tie the tether, and cut each testicle once with one blow, when you have thoroughly skinned them; leave some of the skin of the penis and prepuce which is on the vessels; this manner of castration is better than that done by traction because it leaves no remains of the scrotum from which the animal might want to feel lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Ce sont des animaux qui ont les deux coions et les deux oefs, ou qui portent de chescuns une partie; et par le droit de nature est que li males n'aient pas les vases de la femele en eu cors, ne les females les vases de li males.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	There are two kinds of hermaphrodites among men; one is when a man has something like the image of female genitals between his testicles and it sometimes secretes urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another type occurs in women, situated on the forearm like a rod and two knobs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment for men and women is that you join the chapped skin together, and treat it like other wounds; in the second type, for men whose urine flows through the hide of the knobs, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the swelling.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Swelling is chapped skin on the natural part, so large and ugly to see; some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of the swelling with your hand or pincers, and join it lightly; do not go too deep lest blood flows out, then treat another cure like any other wound until it is healed; and for another type of chapped skin that forms at the mouth of the vagina, expel it, and perhaps fire it, as it resembles cow dung, thus the ancients called it "cow-like disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it off, as we have said for a growth caused by itching, and treat it until it is clean.
de erratique	Of wandering.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Wandering is the case when the woman's nature is not pierced or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth or an accident due to illness that has occurred; whether it is through a joined charm, or subtle touch of evil spirits or species, and it happens perfectly in the womb, on the sides, below, or wherever; and prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps having flowers [childbirth]; and the knowledge of such is by observing the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstructions appear nearby, then they will reach your fingers or rod [instrument].
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of delicate tissue and close to the two lips, hurry up and do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with legs spread; then stretch the two lips widely so that the delicate tissue is round, and covers the openings; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the spot, and make the woman lie to the man every day until it cannot close.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the tissue is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula similar to myrtle leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the obstruction is of flesh that has not yet born hair, suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have ready some medicines to staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with white of egg; then apply a broad leaden plate so the wound cannot close; and let it remain for long enough, and provide a dry linen dressing; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a new flesh grows in the wound, it should be cut according to this method, unless there are embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an embedded abscess in the wound, one must not attempt to cut it open.
des emorroides	Of haemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Haemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually bleed, and when they are old they become thick; I have previously mentioned their similarities to other conditions, and the signs, now I shall speak about those which can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that haemorrhoids and thick growths, when they are completely inside the anus, and cannot be felt, should not be treated with a cauterising iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the swamp, where one can feel, are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore put the woman in a cold house, then extend the ulcer with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if there is an outflow of blood, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, galls, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have him undergo cupping therapy on his back and breasts without hurting them; then take linen, soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the abscess heals, treat the area with ointment until it is cured; and that which is called 'albathir' is red, and resembles a rough head, must be cut as I have said before about the tumor; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of abscess that can occur in the marrow, such as cancer, stone abscess, herpes, tumors, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and several other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which forms in the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that settle low; and if you wish to know the work of iron, then look to see if the abscess is acute at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain is eased; then have the patient sit on a seat, and place two small seats beneath him so that he leans back, supporting his back and gathering together the parts below his legs; and let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms underneath his knees, binding them well with a good bandage. Then suck out towards the right side and introduce the instrument which is used to open the mouth of the abscess, from whence comes its form; and when you wish to introduce this instrument, it is necessary that first you trace an outline so as to know the depth of the abscess, lest what enters into the instrument go in too deeply and injure the patient. If the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the abscess with cloths so that the instrument does not harm him; and let he who holds the instrument place its horn above it while holding onto it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is swollen with pus, you must avoid treating it with hot iron; instead, treat it as we have described in the section on [wound treatment].
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	First, the midwife must know the natural process of childbirth and recognize its signs: when you see the woman's water breaking, and she desires to smell her waters; then be aware that the child is hastening to come out quickly; henceforth, understand that these are natural births, with the infant born headfirst, and the second stage occurring alongside it; and as soon as you see these signs, you must gently press on her belly so the child comes out swiftly; for when its head descends, the second stage begins alongside it, and the mother's uterus is cleansed of excesses by a thorough cleansing process; whereas those born differently are not born naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes happens that he comes onto his feet, and then his body falls forward or backward, and the hands, or he comes down on his belly, often, and is turned by chance over onto his neck, and into other evil positions; so here we need a nurse who is wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deceit, and I shall show you all the positions how one must help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out onto his head by natural delivery, and the woman labours painfully in childbirth, and her strength is weak, then have the midwife sit her on a saddle, where women hold her; and stimulate her nature with some oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, then insert the small spatula between her two hands which looks like this: [describe]
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the caul, and cut at her nail so that the moisture which is within runs out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give an enema to the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then make her sneeze by giving her some sneezing powder, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: now draw out the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands emerge first, you must gently pull them out a little at a time; and if they cannot be pulled out, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet upwards; then lower the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during this process; and if the hands cannot be extracted, and the child is dead, cut open the hands with the knife provided here, and extract the child, pulling evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, push it upwards and then turn it a little at a time until it is level; then take one foot and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it reaches up to the thighs, instruct him to grasp [it] and make him sneeze forcefully; if it is fever, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not fever as we have said, then turn him on his side and side again until he is in his natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he will be lightly dislocated.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if fever does not come as we have said, take the extract of a herb called altea, and oil of sisam, and melted gum, and grind all this in a mortar; place it on the woman's vulva and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to under her armpits; and when she is moistened below, make a myrrh collar for her, and put it underneath, and leave it an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and press her belly gently, because the child will now be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child upon their knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place the nurse's hands here and there; then let them lean on their neck, and hang their feet down, and lay them on the bed; and fold their hands thus and so, and then press their hands onto their stomach, and remove the cushions from beneath, until they are prepared below; and if the child does not suck, take its feet and move it vigorously, then move their belly upwards, then put in all your hands; encourage the child here and there; and tell the woman to hold herself so that the child exits.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child, which comes from the wide part with one hand hanging.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must prepare to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman get up and walk; if she can't walk, make her lie on the bed, and stretch her legs vigorously; then administer the medication that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; encourage the child according to natural form, and make her sneeze, and tell her to hold herself so that the child exits.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the exit of the child onto its neck, and has spread out his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I agree that the nurse should hold his hand, then turn it a little and gently stretch it; and when it is equalized, apply some of the natural muscle ointment we mentioned earlier with oil, then instruct her to move it slowly; and once you have done this, make her sit on a chair, order her to grab onto something, and then make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for every midwife
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out this way for every midwife, pinch the midwife with your nail until all moisture is gone; and if the child falls on his face or neck, pinch him from behind so he doesn't get stuck there, then push the child inside again until you have properly repositioned him, and order the woman to grab something: only then can you gently pull.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the dislocation of the wrists
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born together; this is not a strange occurrence, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Those are strange, and do not live if born thus; I know this, that they be multiplied, and are separated by the sutures which divide them, which is tied to the fontanelle; and sometimes they emerge naturally like a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born severely afflicted, treat them as we have said, and let the nurse be skilled, doing quickly and lightly what is needed; act swiftly for their welfare.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Are made in the year one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or many up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious blood, and it is necessary that the nurse knows all this, for perhaps similar things will happen to her; so she should act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in her belly, as I said in the section above, and there is no progress, and you must perform manual work; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be placed on her back, with her legs elevated, and her feet pointing downwards. The minister should hold two parts to her, or she should be tied to the bed so she cannot move during the procedure. You should then moisten the mouth of the womb with oil, mixed with an infusion of altee, fenugreek, and flax seeds; anoint the hands of the nurse with these oils and mixtures; insert them gently into the womb, first checking that the place where they are inserted is suitable for this purpose. If the child is equipped with its limbs, ensure it descends onto its head; if not, insert the instrument through her eyes, neck, mouth, palate, below the beard, in the armpit or near the sides of the body. If the descent is towards the feet, secure the instrument to the calf and side of the leg. The operator should hold the instrument with their right hand, placing the curve between the two fingers of their left hand; insert it gently into any one of these places we have mentioned until you reach the empty space within her womb. This is what the instrument looks like:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert a second hook against the other edge, or use the third if needed, so that the extraction is equal; and then stretch it equally by moving from one side to the other, to remove it, and let the hooks be serrated to hold it, as this is their form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, anoint the wound with some of your fingers' oil and push it into that part, then pull the other part; and if there is still a point remaining, place this hook or another higher up, and do so until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes in front of the other and you cannot pull it back due to tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it is completely covered; then cut through its jointure at the palm or at the heel, and so you must do for the other hand and foot as well.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is standing on its feet, then there is slight traction, and the guidance to the mouth of the womb is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is trapped in the belly or the breast, then you must extract it with cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut open the belly or the breast so that the moisture which is there flows out; and if other parts have been removed, but the head remains, push its arm up from behind the pubic bone to guide it towards the mouth of the womb; then insert one or two fingers as far in as possible; pull it forth gently; and if the mouth of the womb is constricted due to hot inflammation which has developed there, it should not be disturbed but rather moist and fatty substances must be introduced; and introduce poultices, as well as water-based softening and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on their side, and you can make them lie flat, then manage as we have said for a living child; but if you cannot do this, then cut it up in pieces, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	Once this is done, if it behaves as we have said for hot abscesses that appear in the body; and if there is an outflow of blood, then apply cold compresses to stop it, and treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been dead then another was born on top of it, and the other died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came on her neck, and swelled so much that it opened up, and began to emit a foul smell.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat him, and I thought long, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting plaster, and an bone came out, followed by others after several days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound and withdrew many bones with my hands until the woman felt better; she lived for a long time afterwards with only a small hole where they were taken from; I have recorded this chapter because when masters find something strange, they must know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the marrow back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, which we have with our hands; and at II turning to the II heads of the II arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictive ones, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the trunk should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees one finger wide, and one palm and a half long; and in the middle of the two limbs there are two adjustments of this same wood, which must be firmly fixed on both sides, each being half a palm or slightly more long; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in its likeness, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling a pair of tongs; it shall have at the two jaws two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vulva with all this instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down and her legs spread apart. Then push together the two adjustments into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs. Then operate your hand throughout the instrument as you have done in tongs equally according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the vulva until she achieves what she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely surmounted and their forms are multiplied; when the physician has them prepared, it makes his work quicker and renders him more expert in proportion to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument at your disposal, as their need is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the midwife is restrained during childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze vigorously, and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she faints from this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, make a hole in its lid, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the sufferer, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; cook all these herbs or some of them in water over fire; then attach a cane to the hole in the pot's lid, put the other end into the patient's mouth, and keep it there until the vapors reach inside her; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary injury occurs.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if the swelling remains after this treatment and does not heal, instruct the nurse to dampen her left hand with oil of sesame or muskroot juice, then insert it into the body cavity, seeking the secondary injury; once found, she should grasp and extend it little by little in a straight line, ensuring the injured part is not twisted during extraction; instead, move it gently from side to side before pulling. It will come out easily and set itself free.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the wound is narrow and constricted, we have already mentioned the treatment of inducing coughing and fumigation with herbs; if these methods fail as described above, be careful not to make a mistake while pulling [the arrow]; instead, secure what is at the mouth of the wound to the woman's thigh by binding it there, then administer an ointment enema made from four ingredients: this will rot and loosen the wound, allowing it to heal and eventually close; however, when this happens, a bad smell may arise in the stomach or head, hurting the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to have suitable fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to stop her flowering and menses is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is made of glass resembling a hen's egg, and one places the subtle chief in it over the fire; the fumes are above the charcoal, and let them be consumed until they are gone, then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to perforate the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without the fundament perforated, but have a subtle skin-like covering: so at their bath you must pierce this covering with your finger, not a pointed spatula, and be careful that it is not injured; then place on moist wool soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, insert a piece of lead wire into the hole, and leave it there for several days; remove it when the child wishes to go outdoors.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden closure of a wound or abscess occurs; you must cut away the scar tissue so that it can be treated; as we have mentioned with regard to lead wire.
de la fistule dou fondement	From an anal fistula.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Anal fistulas are caused by inflammation and swelling that originates beneath the anus or in the space between the two parts; there may be one or more fistulas present. When this inflammation is longstanding, it leads to hardening, and sometimes a white, thin worm appears, and occasionally these fistulas penetrate all the way through. They can be recognized due to what comes out with the faeces or flatulence when the patient defecates; perhaps even a worm emerges.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder, and halfway up the penis; reaching as far as the hip joint, and down to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	Thus one can identify whether the fistula pierces through to the anus or not; it is when you insert your index finger into the anus, and gently push a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula where there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is any twisting, insert instead a thin tent of lead or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of excrement, wind, or urine as we have said: know that it does not pierce through; so refrain from treating.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces through to the bladder or the urine duct, it leaks urine, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces through to the hip joint, then the wound reaches there; if there is no tortuosity and the source of pain is found around it, it must be immediately cut away, and neither medicine nor quick-acting ointment can help it; in these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than labour, and the vanity of foolish surgeons who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not penetrating and are not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on their back; you lift their legs up to their hips, and incline their hips towards their belly; then insert a bronze probe or an iron one if there is tortuosity, until you find where the wound reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, you must insert your index finger there, if then you feel that the tendon has been pierced; and be aware of any gap between your finger and the skin or flesh beneath, then know that it is perforated; do not work on this wound as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can indeed heal some of these injuries but this rarely happens; the treatment involves heating a thin cautery according to the width of the fistula as described earlier; insert it hot into the fistula until you reach the anus; repeat this two or three times, until you know that the unhealthy flesh which resembles feathers has been burned away; then treat the wound with wet bandages in butter, so that all the diseased tissue is removed, and dress it daily to heal the skin.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus cured, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be cured otherwise, and if the tent enters but does not pierce through to the rectum at the bottom, place a thick covering of fat or suet between your finger and the tent, so that you see the fistula on which the covering rests; cut into it from the beginning of the fistula and push forward before the tent, then cauterize afterward until it reaches the top of the tent; the tent will be released and fall out. Then remove those faulty pieces of fat, which look like a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood defeats you and escapes between your finger and the work, cauterize it with fire or astringent medication.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization brings together two beneficial effects: namely, the burning of adjacent flesh and the stemming of blood flow as well as drying up moisture; thereafter treating moist sores with butter or crushed substances until the skin turns supple, and once flesh is burned in a suppling manner; finally treat the wound with hot ointments hardening tough flesh, which are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is cured and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula extends to the anus, and is away from the body, put your finger in the anus, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the sore, and there is either skin, sinew or flesh, which is close to breaking through, if you find no sign of improvement or hope by any of the three methods - cauterization as we have said, cutting deeply, or applying a dressing and treating it as before; do not go too deep so that you do not cut the muscle holding the anus together, and defecation comes out unwillingly. Then treat it as we have said, perhaps it will be cured, or remove this membrane and clean when it is cut near the anus, either with a dressing or other pointed instrument; then remove the faulty flesh which is in the wound as much as you can. Then turn to restoring the wound, and preventing the fistula outside of the anus; this would be easier on the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is located on the side of the anus near the skin above, take a perforated probe with a pointed end like this one:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And here you insert the wire bent at right angles in such a way that it enters through one hole and exits from another; then you advance the probe along the entire length of the wire into the fistula until it reaches its end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it perforates the wall of the anus inside, then remove the wire from that orifice so you insert your finger into the anus; and pull out the end of the wire, and bring together the two ends and hold them tight to each other for one day or two; and sometimes bind it until the wire seizes those tissues which are between the two pieces, and they excrete; then treat the wound until it is healed and closed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not rupture, make it perforate by all means possible unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to operate on the wound if it is too deeply embedded and then treat it as we have said until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinalis muscle from which one makes a fistula is very sharp in some places and blunt elsewhere; and on another side it is not so, for this reason do not operate that which should not be operated upon as you see here:
des emorroydes	From the hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus like resin grains, small or large, and with them comes blood; sometimes there is one, others have many. Hemorrhoids can also be outside the anus and at its beginning; but those that are out have little moisture, and instead some yellow water or a bit of blood come from it, they have the color of flesh. As for treatment, if hemorrhoids are inside the anus, tell the patient to strain themselves by going to chamber pot until the anus opens up wide enough so you can see them; hurry quickly and use pincers or your nails to grasp them by their roots then cut them off. If they cannot be grasped with pincers because of their moisture, take a piece of linen cloth, cotton, or chamois leather and pull hemorrhoids out between your fingers before cutting it off; then cover area with hot powder that replaces cauterization as described in the cautery chapter; otherwise you can cauterize as explained there then treat them with other remedies until they heal. If the anus cannot be opened, enema the patient with sharp and bitter enema to wash out what is inside the anus so it can open up freely; when patients feel better and the filaments come out of their anus on its own, treatment will be easier: take hold of them by your nails or pincers then cut them off before treating them as we have said until they heal and avoid cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	To dry up the phlegm or feces from the bowels
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying up of feces in the intestine, due to the constraint of nature and when the illness is old or medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should apply the bark of a spathilia or your nail to the point, preventing it from moistening, and then treat it until it hardens as required; if it cannot harden, resume the shaving more vigorously than before so that it bleeds heavily and becomes raw; then cure it again until healed.
dou fremit	cooling down
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formica is a small erroneous appearance between the skin and flesh that penetrates deeply; sometimes it encounters coldness and one feels, like from cooling down, and it spreads throughout the body, mostly in the hands rather than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane made from a goose quill or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the humerus, so that the purple circles touch the humerus all around; then turn your hand over the entire cane until you grasp it entirely around the humerus, put it in perfectly, and pull out the humerus from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one from a cane of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be hollow below and solid above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so as to hold it with your thumb and forefinger, and squeeze it; And if you wish, cauterize the humerus, just as is explained in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is the silver clyster made nor of tin, nor of molten brass or wrought iron; and never are these instruments small or large but fit to hand.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are fitted for the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffer pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clyster large or small is broad above where the bellies are tied thus:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has an outlet where the bellies are tied as you see and its head is pierced within; and on one side have two holes and on another but one; and where medicines are put in bellies either of animal's bladder or parchment, and are pierced all around with minute apertures, and between each aperture is a thumb-breadth space then fill these apertures with strong thread coiled like X or crisscrossed around, and sew the belly together as is a kid; when medicines are within bind it with a strong thread to instrument in front, then clysterize; and this is form of circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then the ministers squeeze his II hands together until all is visible, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to exit, hold him as much as you can; and if he sleeps a night nearby, so it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him with a stomach illness of obstruction, and the medicine wants to exit prematurely, then restart it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are hemorrhoids at the foundation or abscesses, then let the enema be as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which the skin is tightened:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds; now we will discuss cures involving practical application and medicines according to their use.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and where the wounds are located, as well as what caused them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various things such as striking with stones, sword cuts and stabs from knives, or injuries from lances, sticks, arrows, or similar objects; wounds can also be classified according to where on the body they occur, like a wound on the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, or other parts of the body. I will explain the treatment for each type of wound and begin with simple head wounds since their memory will come up in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, take note if it is due to a stone or similar object, and the skin is still torn with a large wound, and you have slight doubts about an inflamed abscess: then make them bleed immediately using the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be contrary to the injured part; and ensure the patient avoids fullness of wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they do not wish to bleed, let their food be reduced, and drink no wine, nor eat any meat; apply to the wound, should hot abscesses develop, only moist cotton in rose oil or astringent wine; but if there is no hot abscess, then place on the wound, while it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, some powder which I will describe shortly; however, if the air has moved it, apply certain ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with sutures, then bring them together with stitching, as I will explain for wounds of the abdomen, regarding the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed down to the bone, and it bends, and only hangs by a piece of skin, then cut away that piece; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat coarse meats, such as beef and wheat pudding, as well as poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find flesh that is rotten, and it has not reached the bone, then cut away all the rottenness, throw it out, and then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein which will not stop bleeding despite efforts with medicine, then seek out the artery, and if you find it severed, tie it up with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize the artery.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; it is that you apply this powder which seals as soon as the cold has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of the powder is thus: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts live alum, and finely powder them, then apply it to the wound, holding it firmly in place until it dries well and adheres to all its blood; then bind it securely, and leave it without loosening, if there is no swelling; for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only the alum is used when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the cold has moved from the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has cauterized the wound, especially in winter, do not put this powder on it; instead, apply some digestive ointments or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey until it flows freely; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with subtle pincers; I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	Of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no significant difference between this and a head wound; however, if the windpipe or artery in the neck is severed...
