Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When an arrow strikes any of these vital organs, and you see the signs of death that I will tell you about below: you must be wary of extracting this arrow, as many die in such cases; and if these ill omens do not appear, and the arrow is not lodged too deeply, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and ruptures the dura mater above the brain, is scotoma (loss of vision) in one or both eyes, vertigo, redness and swelling around the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion and loss of consciousness, vomiting bile; perhaps also blood flows from the nostrils or ears; perhaps they lose speech and voice; and white moisture resembling pus comes out of the wound, as well as charred flesh; if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment (i.e., surgery), and remove the arrow if it is accessible
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is close to the left nipple, and they feel as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; perhaps the pulse changes like the beat of a drum, and dark blood flows out, coldness and cold sweat come over them, and syncope: know then without doubt that death is descending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that an arrowhead has not penetrated is if there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's colour changes, and they breathe heavily and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls onto the covering of the chest, it is by the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great suffering, and all the shoulder limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls on the stomach, perhaps something undigested may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly and no excrement comes out of the lower intestine, there is little hope for a cure or extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out forcefully, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the face, neck, throat, shoulder, arm, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and legs, as well as similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his arm by the collarbone: I pulled it out and extracted it from another place below the ear's fat, and he was healed without any incident.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And thrust into the eye socket beneath the paper below it with an arrow that had been lodged there and whose point could only be reached through the base of the shaft, which was as long as a turkish bow and made entirely of light iron without barbs; The wound healed and no ill effects resulted.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this was an Arabic arrow with barbs; I waited for the beard to grow back, and then carefully extracted it until finally drawing it out, after which the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew an arrow from a man which was lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days his condition did not change; so I cut into the skin above where it had become embedded, extracted it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow lodged in his back or shoulder, and the wound has healed over it; yet the arrow remains inside him, and it does not alter its natural position, nor does it cause any harm to any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, with an arrow in his face, the wound has healed over it as well; and he remains without suffering great pain or any other significant ailments.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow wound for the king's man, which pierced his nose and was slightly angled to the right; and the arrow was entirely lodged within him - I was called upon to heal him three days after the arrow was shot.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted to touch her with all my might, but I felt nothing; he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead I applied an attractive digestive plaster over it so that the flesh wouldn't swell, and there appeared the flesh of the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for several days, and the wound closed up again immediately, but the patient remained ill for a long time until he felt the arrowhead inside his nose one day, and he told me this himself.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it opened up again and I tried to feel around for the arrowhead, sensing its tip in the open flesh; then with that corrosive medicine, I widened the opening of the wound so far as the shaft of the arrowhead became visible to me; and after this process took about four months, the wound then expanded so much that I inserted a pair of pincers inside it, grasping from either side, but could not remove [the arrowhead]; thus I did not cease experimenting with all kinds of instruments until one day I grabbed it successfully using specially designed pincers according to a design described later in this chapter; and finally extracted the arrowhead.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; so I restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you focus your care on what I do not mention, because books cannot cover everything; but wise masters observe very little and understand a lot, and for what is present and lacking, they invent new methods and instruments, to address strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the members in which they are embedded except through two methods: either by the path of entry or through another part; and one that comes out by where it entered is an arrow penetrating fleshy tissue, and this sometimes happens now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her be left until the flesh around is rotten and the exit is relieved; and also, if she is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, leave her there for some days and move her each day; then she will leap out, and if she does not, pierce all around with a very fine awl until the tissue around is widened, and then pull her out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head and goes right up to one of the brains ventricles, and any of the accidents I have mentioned occur to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until after some days when it becomes even, because if the arrow comes up through the skin, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone, and does not come out through the skin, and the patient remains well for a few days without any bad incidents, then devise a way to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted through the skin alone, then apply caustic substances around it, as I have told you; afterward, treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged inside the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the entire wound; and if you can feel it, then extract it with a suitable instrument; but if you are unable to due to the tightness of the wound, or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein involved, then cut open the flesh until the wound is wide enough; remove the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs preventing its removal, carefully cut away the tissue that surrounds them on either side as far as possible, and then break or bend those barbs so that you can extract the arrow; do this carefully to avoid breaking the arrow, for that would make its retrieval much more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding tissue is rotten, then pull it out, for its extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, bring about what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve and opening a vein, and use any means possible to remove the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how he was positioned when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from elsewhere and does not show anything of itself, but the skin is swollen where it lies if you see or feel it clearly: cut above until the tongs can grasp it, then extract it; this will now be easy.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained within the bone, rotate your hand circularly until you enter into the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot come out, leave it alone for now and then restart the extraction process until it comes out; and if there is an arrow within the shaft, push it through the whole shaft; and if it were blunt and you must administer a pushing action, insert an instrument that has been sharpened so that the point of the arrow enters the sharpening of the instrument; then push it forward, and if the arrow is already sharpened, insert the instrument with its point entering first in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all of the flesh around it if possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or thigh or stomach or bladder or flank, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then do so; be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, then extract [the arrow] and sew up the wound if necessary; treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form [shape]:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the driving instrument is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as here [the figure] shows its form.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pincers to use for insertion and extraction is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins through which one is bled are thirty-one in number and sixteen of these are on the head: two veins that lie behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries which are found in the temples where they can be seen; and two veins lying below the eyelids (which run along the inner edge) which are known as "aspires" ; and a vein which lies between the forehead and skull; and the vein that is at the root of nose; and the two jugulars in the neck; and the two veins situated on either side above the lips, these being called "augeherich"; and two veins located beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly used for healing are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which lies on the left side; lay people call it the "vein of the head." The median vein is called the "fast" by lay people and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins. Lay people name this combination as the "vein of the heart." The basilic vein lies on the right side, which lay people call the "belly vein," and it is located above the elbow; this is the vein that appears clearly in the arm pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The safeten vein is the one that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, it has two branches; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one lies under the bend of the arm on the left side, the second sophen which is at the ankle on the right side; the vein called "nesse", which is located at the other ankle; and in the other leg are three more veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins located behind the ears assists in treating longstanding catarrh and migraine; and regarding the characteristics of bleeding, as I mentioned to you, it entails that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a coarse cloth; then hold the patient's neck tight against a pillow, so that the two veins show behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: press them thus between your thumb and forefinger; then where you feel a pulse under your finger, make an incision therewith; next take the lancet, and thrust it beneath the vein down to the bone, then lift up your hand with all the speed possible over the whole length of the vein, and cut both the skin and the vein transversely with two fingers' breadth, making the incision issue blood as much as you wish; then bind it up tightly until it is healed; I have already described the procedure for incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries located in the temples is effective for chronic migraine headaches and acute ophthalmia and for the body of tears from eyes. And here are the qualities of bloodletting as I say: The patient must extend their neck so that the two veins are clearly exposed; feel the pulse beneath your thumb, then bleed above this point; raise the heart upwards onto the vein at your index finger, insert the lancet underneath and raise the vein upwardly, cutting it like you have done for the other two veins and allow blood to flow according to your needs. Then release the patient, and put your thumb over the vein for an hour before applying cotton, then bind firmly and leave until it is healed; we discussed their incision and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is just as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for treating old facial ailments, headaches, and rashes; its quality being that the patient tightens their neck by turning it, so much so that the vein appears; then take the instrument called a "fosseur," whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point over the vein and press it down with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow out according to the desired quantity; then release the patient's neck and bind the wound until it is healed, never working over a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too sharp and it should bleed diagonally, as the bone is close by, and by chance may break the flame if it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the armpit helps with eye issues, scabies, redness, itchiness in the eyes, and facial diseases; the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient should tighten their neck by twisting it with a cloth, as mentioned before; then bleed them, and let the blood flow from side to side, slightly above the armpit but not too far away, for there is no meat there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are delicate, they may break; then let the blood flow out until you have what you need, and then bind it with cotton, tying it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fever, severe head trauma, and facial diseases such as migraine and redness that occurs on the face, especially when it is an old ailment; the quality of this bleeding is as follows: have the patient tighten their neck, then grab your nose with your left hand, take the delicate long vein, and insert it into the space between the two nostrils in the lip, for the vein does not open well towards the front, and the blood will start to flow now; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, as it heals quickly; this is the form of the vein:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the two jugulars helps with narrowing the armpit, starting a boil, many diseases, abscesses, ulcers, herpes, and tumors; the quality of the bloodletting is such that the patient should straighten their neck underneath either side as we have said, and let the master be standing by the head of the patient and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein along its length for about one palm width widely, then draw off the blood moderately or however much is necessary; next repeat likewise in the other vein, then untie the tie, and press gently around both veins so that the patient does not choke; leave him until morning when the wound will have healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bloodletting of the lips,
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of veins above the lips aids in healing mouth sores, gum disease, cracked lips, and their surroundings.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Have the patient sit before you and hold their neck tightly as I've instructed; then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are known by being black and having small dark veins around them: so cut each of these, and if you don't know or doubt, cut the larger of both, and do likewise with the two above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding below the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of the veins that are below the tongue is helpful after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the eye, and for mouth ailments; and the quality of the blood-letting should be such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, you lift their tongue, and look beneath each side a black vein: so bleed one and the other, but do not go too deep, as underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by making a very wide gash with a flat-edged knife, or with an olivewood-handled sharp lancet, which is called "anesil"; and they are broad or narrow according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of St Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the knotted veins full of thick blood that contains dark red and cloudy matter; this is the form of St. Olive's flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed, slender, and for bleeding delicate veins or when there is delicate yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that affect the throat, neck, stomach and belly; and when the bleeder must take care to avoid the artery beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows abundantly, it must be stanched as I said; and the flame should not be held still but moved like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, you must extract it and replace it with another; or take a part of it, or heal the vein in its place in the arm: it opens clearly; and apply flame to the wound as we have said before.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the wound, you must either draw out the arm until you can feel the pulse in that spot; then mark the place and bind up the arm, and apply flame to the wound as we have said before; and be wary not to cut into the artery when you see the area swelling, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: be quick then, and place your finger upon it for a while, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind up the arm and leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; and be afraid, and do not let them move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overpowers you, and there are no medical practitioners present, then cut the artery if it appears open, for this will stop its flow; and stem the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fustic bark, split it open, and take one half, bind this over the wound until tomorrow; if bleeding has stopped, that is good; but should it continue, then treat as already mentioned with staunching powders; and note that staunching may be less effective in some conditions due to the small size of the wound or the strength of the patient's arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the median vein is helpful as it drains blood from above the head and below the body, because this vein combines the basilic and cephalic veins, as mentioned earlier; and during bleeding, watch out for the nerve which lies underneath, and if you cut too deep and hit the nerve, swelling may occur along with numbness, and healing might be difficult; now this nerve often appears but sometimes it doesn't due to its subtlety in some people, so you must then treat it gently with an anaesthetic instrument; remove any part of the nerve that you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a wound between the two nerves, make it longer with a cut.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the superficial temporal artery is helpful as it draws blood from the head and assists the eyes; and one should bleed by making an incision with a hollow olivewood arrow or a myrtle shaft, for this is the safest among all veins, because beneath it there are no nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nonetheless, one should seek the lightest place and not cause any harm if it fails the first time, just start again; perhaps for some people the site swells when pricked the first time, but this is of no consequence.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not administered except to preserve health and avoid future illnesses; the bloodletting should be done in one of three veins which are: namely, cephalic, superficial, and median cubital; and one should bloodlet at the beginning of Lent on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; and one should bloodlet either on the first or third day, two to three hours after the meal.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting administered for illnesses does not have a determined time of day but rather when needed, at any hour and all times; one should not bloodlet children under fourteen years old, nor pregnant women from the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to bleed the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, regardless of the method, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a light clyster, if there is an excess of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful superfluities from the intestines into the principal limbs; one should also not bleed those who are excessively filled with meat, or drunk, until they have sobered up, nor those suffering from dropsy; and it is inadvisable to bleed someone after a bout of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse, hard labor, lack of sleep, fasting, or exhaustion due to any physical exertion; then purify the humors by thinning out the blood with meat, drink, and medicine if you have them at your disposal; then enter the bath, provided that nothing prohibits it, to thin the blood, and bleed from a vein on the back of the arm just above the elbow as we have said before; further, one must refrain from hard labor, exertion, lust, and similar things during this day; be calm and joyful, and let the patient lie down while the bleeder stand over them, then rub the arm twice or thrice, then tie a ligature moderately tight around it, for if it is too loose or tight, blood will not flow through it properly; thereafter one must rub the area with their hands until the veins swell up and can be felt; next moisten the blade with some old oil before applying its tip to the vein slightly below where you wish to bleed so that there will be no damage when it is punctured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are wounds that leak like ropes into the drain, and some are filled with windiness, so when one applies the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the wound; thus, one is in this situation; and if one opens the wound, it is too narrow, for which the surgeons must be mindful of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the wound opens on the first attempt, it is good; if not, try again a little lower or higher, unless the site is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the site is swollen and the patient becomes afraid, leave it for one or two days, do not bind the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will arise; do not enter the bath, then repeat the procedure if it pleases you; and if the aperture is small, let out blood discreetly and doubt that it won't come as much blood as you wish, be fierce with this same aperture until all flame directly; work a little higher, rather than where the site is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, but apply a poultice of oil-soaked linen, for it lightens the body's blood, and the linen that is oily is beneficial in this place; thus administer the oil-soaked linen in each wound you treat to stem the flow of blood, and the same holds true for triacle and eggs, when applied to the place: they are so subtle as to thin the blood and separate it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there arises a large abscess, which happens frequently, especially when it has not been treated before or the opening of the wound is small, then hasten and apply to the place moist sponge in water and saltpetre slightly warm, and hold it tight for an hour; this must be done after the flow of blood from the wound ceases, and if there remains at the place some blackness or greenness over a few days, it does no harm; but if you see it spreading, apply something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in galbanum juice, madder, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	For many times an abscess and appearance happen at the wound of the temple: therefore place your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then this is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So abstain from placing anything on it of what we have said, for perhaps there is a cut in the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person's blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, then let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for the one who is full-bodied and robust, requiring blood extraction, a wider wound must be made, with broad flames; whereas in the case of the feeble patient, do the opposite: bleed them gently but frequently, and perform this bleeding by cutting across rather than pricking; this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive loss of blood or severing nerves, and better than that which cuts lengthwise or crosswise.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If the patient's body requires bleeding, give them bread moistened in pomegranate juice; if they are heated [i.e., too hot], withdraw blood three or four times; and for a cold-complexioned patient, give them moistened bread with treacle syrup, or spiced honey syrup containing pepper, cinnamon, ginger and chickpeas, before bleeding.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the treatment, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks meat broth, and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to draw out the arm, and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And for those who wish to draw out the arm after the first bleeding, and have a strong body, they should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And for those who wish to be bled elsewhere, they should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has too much blood within the body which is already heated and causes fever; one must extract a great quantity of it, and enlarge the opening until it stops with pressure; then you fulfill all conditions for healing, and place your hand on his pulse as he heals so that death does not come instead of relief, and this happens many times when healers are negligent; and it is not good when you wish to unbind the arm and make blood flow a second time, if the opening is closed then do not press strongly upon it, nor if it is curved extend his arm quickly for this would be bad, but leave him until he heals the second time or prick him at the end of the wound so that the congealed blood flows out from the vein's opening and place on it a poultice soaked in water and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, let it drain from the same place, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arm is drained in place of the vein of the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of draining is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the flesh turns red; then it should be bound loosely so that the vein appears clearly, and now let the blood drain horizontally, not lengthwise or widthwise; the opening must be wide, and the draining should occur very close to the joint of the hand, if no more blood can come out, immerse the hand again in warm water and let the blood flow into it until you have enough; but if this is during winter, do not re-immerse the hand in warm water as we use more warm water during summer than winter; and draining from this vein is safer than any other veins for there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the right arm's veins is beneficial for all liver diseases and here is how it works: stretch out the hand, immerse it in hot water until the vein becomes swollen if visible; and if the vein lies across [the hand], and you cut through it entirely, nothing bad will happen. Do not go too deep because the nerves are just beneath the flesh and then return the hand to hot water if the blood has congealed in the wound and cannot exit.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	Once you have extracted as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and lint to the vein in order to seal it; do this for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of the left arm's veins is beneficial for all spleen diseases; do this in the same way as I told you to do on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is valuable for all diseases below the body, such as illnesses of the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments of the thighs and legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient should submerge their foot in hot water, rub over the vein until it ruptures, and bind above the ankle joint; this vein is at the ankle, and extends upwards along the leg to the kidney; bleed either the wider part of the kidney or at the ankle, whichever is easier.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it over the leg, be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and bleed it transversely like when cutting; let the flame be small.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, return the foot to the water and allow the vein to be thoroughly emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the vein is not successfully opened on the first attempt, try again a little higher, for the skin there is salty; do not doubt it is nerve as we have said, and proceed likewise with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the back of the ankle, and its evacuation serves to relieve hip pain when caused by hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The nature of its evacuation is such that the patient should enter the bath and tightly squeeze above the ankle for four turns, as otherwise it will not open the vein; if it opens then thoroughly evacuate all blood possible by drawing across the vein, it may be necessary to cut into it since the skin is salty there, and this vein has a tendency to clot in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot find it, then treat the line that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; make sure the blood flows out as much as possible, then untie the ligature, place cotton on top, and hold it firm; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping incisions.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping devices are made of horn, or brass, or glass; cupping is performed in two ways: either by drawing out blood, or without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this bloodless cupping is done in two ways: either by applying full heat or without heat; the method which draws out blood through incisions is performed on fourteen parts of the body, namely one is at the top of the head; another is on the neck; and two are on each side of the neck; a cup is placed below the chin; and cups are placed on both shoulders; and cups go over the loins; and cups are applied to both arms; and cups are used on both legs; and cups cover both ankles; and this type of cupping draws out only small amounts of blood from tiny veins in the flesh, unlike venesection; there should be no weakening of the patient as happens with venesection; neither full heat nor without heat methods should be administered to any sickness that results from excess or fullness, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness or for acclimatization, we administer cupping every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and during each season; as there are some who experience a heavy head when in need of cupping; while others suffer from fullness, redness on their face, neck and head, darkening around the eyes; there are those who find blood droplets in their mouth, with swollen tongues and coughing up blood; and still others who have dreams, seeing through the night blood, wounds, death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the middle of the month, we instruct them to cup themselves after three hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches... that affect the eyes, and should not be done after evacuating all over the body; this cupping is in place of bleeding from the head, and it is not suitable for those of a cold complexion or who have catarrh, as it does them great harm; therefore it must also not be used by the elderly or those with cold diseases on their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetting.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The cupping in the neck is instead of bleeding the head and the temple, and for that reason it helps with narrowing of the chest, splitting of the lung channel, coughs, and fullness; it should be applied gently because if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping at the two collarbones is beneficial for headaches, eye inflammation, migraines, suffocation, and tooth root pain, and it takes the place of bleeding from the temple; you must tell the healer to press their hand when applying it, so as not to rupture an artery or cause excessive blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The swellings beneath the chin are caused by mouth ailments, and gum infections, and similar conditions that occur in the mouth; they take place between the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The swellings of the shoulders are attributed to ailments caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swellings of the armpits are akin to those in three veins of the arm, as they draw blood from these large vessels; and instruct the healer not to wound them too deeply, for there is bare flesh below, covering nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is above the buttocks relates to haemorrhoids in the anus, and ailments below, it should be large, made of bronze, requiring a good suction; perhaps if it was thin, it would break; and this causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs are clearly beneficial, as they draw blood from the entire body, and they help with long-standing pains in the kidneys, uterus, bladder, and remedy flatulence; they should be placed at two sophens (the hollows behind each knee), and both ankles, yet after long use they weaken the body and cause swooning in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is to first place it on an empty stomach, and suck gently at first, then press firmly, moving evenly, and do not cease until you see the area reddened and swollen, with the appearance of blood redness; then let go, replace the cups, and be mindful of the constitution of the body, for some have tough skin, others delicate: one must strike only once, making broad wounds, but rather shallow; suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, you must strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, you must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out the thick and thin blood, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out a lot of blood, we strike often; and if the blood is dense, you strike perfectly, and the result is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for him who has thick skin and hard, and those with narrow pores, to anoint the cupping glass rims with an aperitif and dissolutive oil: if in summer, violet oil, almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if in winter, cress oil, lily, chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or balsam-oil, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it must be washed after the fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry juice, or pumpkin water, or china root water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with much moisture, it rises easily with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with large excesses, it is raised with old wine, or juice of figs, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or others like these; and one should not be bled by cupping either before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours; and they must not sleep after the fomentation, rather they should sit upright when being cupped and after having been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch out if the person who is healing is choleric, and if their blood is too sharp and inflamed; they must take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and lettuce in moderation, and similar items; and eat little pork, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold complexion, they should take honey syrup and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little pork, few small birds, and pigeons; and on the day they undergo cupping, they must drink more than eat; and sometimes it is necessary to give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping, in order to strengthen the principal limbs; and although the blood may be thin, those who are hot should not drink these things.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are applied without causing injury are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, podagra, and on the abdomen, hip, kidneys, and groin, because these members cannot bear any wounding over their ulcers; nor is it done for anything other than to draw blood from limb to limb as we do when placing them on the breasts in order to heal a newborn child; to remove the viscosity that exists within the member, just as we place cups on the abdomen and hip to reduce swelling of these members; and to relieve pain where there are calculi or stones, perhaps by extracting the calculus through its attractive virtue or moving the stone from its position; and thus it acts when applied to the liver and spleen in cases of retained flatus, and such cups are administered empty for only sucking; and sometimes they are administered along with fire, and other times filled with warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with warm water alone or with water into which appropriate herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has a width of two fingers and a depth of half a palm, and on its side, near the middle, there is a small hole just big enough to insert a needle, and it should be made of copper, soft in front so as not to hurt the patient when applied to the body; and at its center, there should be an iron or metal rod for placing a burning candle, and they come in different sizes: large and small according to the ailments and ages of those who use them; because cupping glasses for children are different from those used on the elderly, and those for thin people differ from those for obese.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One should thus place this cupping glass on the body in the following manner: take a wax candle or a piece of linen and put it into the cupping glass through the iron rod that is inside it, so that the flame is at its base, away from the patient's skin; then place the cupping glass on the affected part of the body, ensuring your two fingers cover the hole we mentioned earlier, allowing you to control the vapor as needed and remove the cupping glass when necessary; take the linen and repeat this process often if required.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment administered for pleurisy, which is always acute, there is no tube or aperture, and it is only applied when full of water, being placed directly on the limb; its form is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.
