And if it is the large bone that is broken, one should pull on it more firmly and stretch it; hold the end of the limb with one hand higher than the others, and keep the small fingers lower than the other fingers; have the patient cross their arms over themselves, and place a pillow in front of them at a height where they feel no strain. Then let two ministers support the injured person's arm from below near the wrist or elbow, and another minister support it from above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the mirror in front of them evenly so they see their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, place each one back in its place and grasp the heart of any piece that cannot be restored to its original position; then cut it away as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken bone there is also a wound, as I have spoken of it in the singular chapter, then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration process hot abscesses appear, take some cerote made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; bind this cloth over it gently until the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote and apply an ointment made of mill powder with plenty of egg, then place the splints, ensuring that the splint over the broken bone is closest and somewhat wider than the others; know that there must be six splints on each arm in different arrangements depending on which bones are broken or not: whether one or two. Bind it tighter near the fracture than elsewhere and always more loosely as you move away from it, as I said at the beginning of this chapter. The cloths over the break should be soft and moist, never hard nor rough; and the thread used to bind them must not be too thick nor too thin, as we have mentioned.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident befalls the limb, such as itching which occurs in limbs, you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and leave the limb not too tight at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then restart the tightening process, and if the ligament is softened and the bones are separated or similar, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you observe that nourishment cannot reach the limb due to its tightness, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days until circulation flows again; then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, do not release them until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If all around is quiet, then bind their hands to their neck, and keep their necks even, avoiding any movement or turning, and let them sleep on their back; know that this fracture will be healed in 30 days or 35, perhaps even in 20 days depending on the composition of ingredients and the patient's constitution.
de la brisure de la main	On the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather it is more often a dislocation.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged, and sits upright in front of them evenly; then place their hand on a flat surface, and the minister extends the broken bones, setting them level with one another until they are properly aligned; apply a plaster cast and bandages, unless an abscess arises, then put a splint according to the location; it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the front of the shinbone, make a circle of cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it tightly to their broken shin; then take a long strip of cloth, and let the heart-shaped pad be as large as the palm of your hand, and bind it securely, as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must put a pad above and another below the broken bone, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and secure the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, be it the thumb, then set it evenly as required; and bind it with the hand, and see to put a small straight pad to raise the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, then set them evenly, and bind it with the healthy finger next to it; or you may bind them all together, holding them in an "I" shape, which works better, or you can put a pad on top, like for the thumb; and take care in the restoration and arrangement regarding hot abscesses, and assist those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it can be clearly seen when the leg turns forward or backward; the restoration involves binding one ligament above and another below the fracture.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each assistant stretches out their binding to an equal part; this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh bone, one binding should be towards the armpit, and the other bindings below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if the fracture is near the knee, then the bindings should be alongside the knee, and the stretching should be downwards; next, the assistants place the bone in its natural position with both hands, ensuring it aligns correctly, before applying a plaster cast and securing it, unless an abscess occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down before returning to your work and treatment; the dressing is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap the fracture with I thick bandage doubled to II or III layers, leaving the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes up to the groin, and thread I long wire between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the wire above; then wrap the bandage around the leg and thigh, and place splints over the fracture, placing a splint over the bone of the leg; then fill the void between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to even out the pressure, then start tying firmly III or IV turns over the fracture; as you go up from the fracture, lessen the tightness; then take hold of I end of the wire you threaded between the leg and thigh, and tie it to III splints above, then return to below at the other end of the wire, until you reach beside the foot; tighten so that it cannot move from its place, then leave it like this, ensuring no abscess, swelling or other complication develops.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then dislocate it and address what comes next, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that grip, it must be removed, if possible; and if one cannot, then the place must be split open, and force it out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that one sets it with pins, as in the shoulder and arm; however, when restoring it in this manner, the patient does not suffer discomfort.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in twenty days, or perhaps a little less or more, depending on the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the groove of the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee alley there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is but a crack or hole, and this happens with any wound, both wounded and unwounded, and one feels good about it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is such that one sets the equal of what is round to its two sides so they are assembled as close as possible; then apply the plaster, and insert a round peg if needed, and tighten it accordingly, then observe all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, like hot abscesses and similar ones; assign each accident what suits it until healing.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is broken, return to the previous step.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible; return underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, provide an extension and make it equal, binding the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is severe and there are multiple fragments, let the extension be lesser and more gentle; adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of wood, padded on the inside, that wrap around the leg from one side to the other, extending from just above the knee down; then wrap two bandages around it in two layers, binding them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot bend right or left. This is good, and some use a splint of wood along the length of the leg to prevent movement, properly applied at the fracture site or where there is an open wound; move the leg each day to check for abscesses or other complications, treating it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the bones of the foot, there can be breaks and bruises, and sometimes only a sprain in various conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were about to walk, then put your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, press them until they return to their places; then apply a plaster cast and bandage it, place a small tablet with two fingers' worth of [substance] underneath the belly of the foot, secure it to the foot appropriately, wrap it with cloth and other necessary materials.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place in the broken toe a peg according to its length, and let it be slightly wider, then put beneath the foot that board I mentioned, and strain it appropriately; if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a peg according to its measure, wrapped in a linen cloth, and secure the board beneath the foot; and let it extend over the head of the board from outside the stomach of the foot so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said regarding other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and help each accident as it is required.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make the woman sit with her legs wide apart, then bend her towards the back part and have someone hold her from behind; then fill the vaginal opening of the patient's nature with cotton wadding until it is full; get some pebbles and put them inside too so they are surrounded by the cotton; stand up the woman carefully lifting her slightly upwards several times to shake down the stones, and when the cotton comes out at the entrance of the vagina you will see that the bones have come together again with the help of the stones; then when she wishes to urinate take away the cotton wadding until after she has passed water it is replaced. Do this for seven days or thereabouts: the fracture should be healed, and if you wish to hasten recovery get a sheep's bladder tie one end of a cane to its opening, fill the whole thing with air by blowing through the other end, then insert the inflated bladder in the woman's vagina; blow hard into the cane so that the bladder becomes thoroughly distended inside her: the vaginal walls will thus be brought together again and the fracture healed. Then pack some cotton wadding round it for a few days until the parts are healed
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who applies study and practice to them, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break indicates in many ways the correct path to restoration: understand this, then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's windpipe and insert it inside the penis; then wrap it with cloth around, and leave it for three days there, and it will swiftly heal.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaks that have wounds.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with wounds, especially if it's large like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, to be healed swiftly, as the healings we have discussed attest to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply vitriol to staunch it, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture that same hour or day, unless a hot abscess comes about.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If a hot abscess does occur, leave the restoration for nine days until the abscess is alleviated, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, as you would bring about an ill outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on an uncovered heart, you must set it gently with your hands in slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension does not align with your hands, reset it with this iron instrument which is seven or eight fingers long and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this, three or four are needed depending on what is necessary in each bone-setting cure; and let it be round and a little thick so that it does not bend under compression on the limb being treated, and sharpened at the end, and thickened toward the middle thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palanching," for this reason the bent head must be placed on top of the protruding bone, and push once until it returns to its place, and ensure they are aligned with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot grasp the bone properly, then you must cut away the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it away with an appropriate instrument, whether chisel or knife, to your ability; remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not yet in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si ensure it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black styptic wine, and properly so if it is in the east; and do not put on the wound any ointment or other oily substance, for it would cause rot and corruption; then apply stars once you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and cut away all covering around according to the size of the wound, taking great care that the wound is not constrained by the fracture; this mistake has often been made by foolish surgeons, causing harm or death in some cases; and ensure that the bindings are looser than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is severe or large, and you fear a bad outcome as mentioned earlier, and find pain in that spot, then do not apply stars but instead wrap it tightly with hard cloths and tie them securely.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see swelling after one or two days at the wound, remove what you have placed on it entirely, and apply healing ointment such as Tetraconion and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is fused and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And ensure that the limb is bandaged in such a way that the swelling runs down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if after many days it still does not heal but swells again, know that there are small bone fragments present, which is why you must probe the wound with a needle, and remove all these dislocated pieces causing pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms there, or any other kind of corruption occurs, then you must treat it according to what he says in his chapter previously mentioned.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and protruding from the limb, like the thighbone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for many times this leads to death, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, simply leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	wounds that arise over the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see patients after the healing of a break, especially when it is near a joint, and it's an ugly sight to see the figure of the limb; perhaps they can no longer perform their natural functions with that limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed therefore if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, gum Arabic, galbanum and other similar remedies; mix one or all of these with a styptic wine or egg white or milk of almonds; wrap it in lint on a compress, hold tight without loosening for some days then replace the dressing again until nodation is gone; or lay on a well-made piece of lead because its property is to reduce swellings from limbs and if the nodation has already hardened like stone you will have to chisel off the superfluous matter or use a rasp until it is removed, and cure it so that it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	From the member which is weak after recovery.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and feeble, it occurs due to many causes: one of which is being bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or having too many bindings, preventing nourishment from reaching the member; or excessive bleeding; or large movements, not at the right time; or a lack of blood in the body, thus making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body so that blood multiplies within it; administer baths, and give joy and leisure; then apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment draws in great nourishment, and often moisten with warm water until nourishment reaches the member; and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of a twisted limb after injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bone is still visible, and the shape of the limb is unattractive, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those foolish people who say that you should break the limb again from scratch; many such things have happened in our land, and these procedures are blamed for causing great harm and even death. However, if the knots and bruises are fresh, they should be soaked with hot water or cooked softening herbs, like leaves of mallow, roots, marshmallow root, and similar things; apply a softening plaster, like well-made diaquartz, mix the mucilage of mallow with goose fat or sesame oil and make an ointment from it; alternatively you can take fatty figs, crush them with colon fiber, and any other medicines that ease inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodule is removed by continually and extensively rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And provide gentle movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the curvature is severe and hardened like stone, and it must be removed with an iron tool, then one must cut down to the bone using a delicate knife; and insert a suture and focus on the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one must promptly reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the joint swells, and by chance it may be replaced with pain; therefore, it must not be moved when swollen: many times this brings on spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this occurs, make the patient bleed, then leave them alone until the abscess is healed; then bathe the limb in warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as it comes back into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes jaws become dislocated on both sides, and there are two types of dislocation: either they are slightly out of place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, with saliva running from the mouth which cannot be contained, nor can they close their mouths, and their speech is slurred.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is minor, it can often return through various adjustments.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and fully displaced, you must reposition it swiftly without delay; in such a manner that your assistant holds the patient's head, and pushes one of their hands' fingers into the root of the dislocation within the mouth, if the dislocation involves two parts; the other hand's fingers should be outside to provide balance; instruct the patient to relax their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The practitioner then places it evenly until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if repositioning is difficult, especially when both mandibles are involved together, warm them with hot water and oil until they can be gently eased back into place; do not delay the process of returning them as we have instructed.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's wound is closed without softening it, apply moistened dressings soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax; then lightly bind it with soft bandages. Let the patient sleep on their back, with two pillows under their shoulders to prevent any movement to the right or left, and let them avoid straining during chewing; but feed him light food until his pain is relieved and his jaws are healed. Then allow him to eat what he wants lightly, and do not exert himself in opening his mouth for eating or drinking until his jaw is well-healed and strengthened.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their original position within an hour and do not return to their proper place, fever and constant pain will result; possibly leading to diarrhea, or perhaps vomiting clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and often does the person die whom it befalls, within nine days.
de la forcelle	From the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from the inside of its shaft or below, and is sometimes dislocated outwards, which one can easily tell.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on their back and extends their arms; then you press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply a plaster and bandage, holding it tight; and the shoulder which faces away from the blade cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it does dislocate at some point, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, binding it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; likewise is the head of the shoulder restored when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: first, it dislocates at the joint below; secondly, at the part of the chest; and occasionally, it dislocates above, which happens rarely; it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside due to nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the joint, especially in those with little flesh, as it easily jumps out for them; for those with enough flesh, it jumps out with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally happens to some men a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is recognized as dislocation when it points towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one; you will find an obvious distinction between them; and at the head of the shoulder, a pit, under the armpit against which lies the head of the shoulder, like an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move in any way; similarly if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly feel it on touch; this type of dislocation is easy to reset when it is new or affecting a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is as follows: have the assistant lift the patient's hand upwards, then place your palms underneath the armpit, and raise the joint forcefully to its position above; let the assistants lift and stretch out the hand upwards before placing it below; this will cause a stir.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said with manual traction on the same day, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and administer a gentle softening and soothing remedy, such as a decoction of altee, fenugreek, and mellilote in water, and let him drink this; then remind the patient to lie on his back, and place beneath him an even woolen cushion, neither too soft nor too hard; then have the assistant place their heel on the cushion, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, pulling the patient's hand; while another assistant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder returns at once, and if you wish to reset it in this way: ensure there is a taller man present than the patient; have him stand upright by the side, pushing the patient's shoulder under the cushion from below, lifting the cushion upwards so that the patient hangs in mid-air; while another assistant pulls the patient's hand downwards towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, weigh them down with something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	We also reset it in another way: take a long pole and plant it in the ground so that the shoulder is as high as the pistol, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it underneath the patient, but have soft coverings on top of him, and let the patient's arm rest along the length of the log; then stretch his hand downward on the other side quite strongly, and the joint will come back into its place quickly; if it does not wish to return with all these things we have said, do this cure: take a pole two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a rounded top so you can perfectly insert it underneath the shoulder bone, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay upon the head of the sick person a soft cloth so that the wood does not hurt them, then place the patient under the bench; and extend their arm along the long side of the wooden block, and tie the shoulder to the block, and the arm to the head with the hand, then put the arm on the edge of a wide stool, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, you must put under the bench an equal woolen pad, then apply a plaster prepared with flour powder, incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it; then strap it underneath the bench appropriately, and turn the bandage back onto the plaster, embrace the hand to their neck, and let the hands stay thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And one should eat little, so that the limb is strengthened, for it will heal quicker; then increase eating after five or seven days, and move it; if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place due to moisture that has entered it or for another reason, then you must apply cauterization to three openings, as mentioned before in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and they cannot lift their arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut, stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be properly set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that affects the hip and breasts from behind is caused by a push or pull of hands and is treated elsewhere; treat it until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process, the limb develops cracks and moves slowly, the patient should bathe frequently until these cracks are alleviated and return to their original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of shoulder dislocation:
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint can be dislocated partially and returns partially; if it is completely dislocated, especially in front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected because it is visible and felt well; it dislocates according to each person's build.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick man's wound with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm or reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before any abscesses form, because if an abscess forms, it will be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, causes greater pain, and in some cases, leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	The restoration process is as follows: when it can be reset, extend their arm with both your hands; have their arms spread out, and place your hands around the affected area from above and below, pushing the joint back into its socket or towards the root of the palm until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it occurs when one doubles over their hand to their hand, and it strains the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; those who assist should stretch the arm and bend it with two hands so that there is no movement during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, having wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it beforehand; when you have aligned the joint with their hand, anoint it with oil to soften the joint, then manipulate the joint firmly until it returns; once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white on top, straining it tightly, and fasten the arm to the patient's neck for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and leave it; but if you see that the joint does not hold well, redo the poultice and the bandage, and leave it like this for a few days until it is securely set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels tenderness after the joint is reset, and it changes, bathe him and gently rub the area until it becomes soothing; or apply a layer of fatty sheep's wool to the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and place him in a bath; once he sweats, gently massage his joints, then reapply the wool, and put him back into the bath; do this twice or three times until it is healed. If you can see any white fatty tissue, apply warm beef tallow with butter to the strain above it will return to its normal position
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The wrist is dislocated and its return is light, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be reset immediately when dislocated, unless the place is swollen or an abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the method of resetting is that you place the affected hand on a table, and have the assistants stretch out the hand, and adjust it so that they put their palm over the apparent joint, and push until it returns. However, one must ensure it is properly aligned; therefore, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table and let the assistants put their hand over the apparent joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; if not, apply a strain of emollient plasters to soothe hot abscesses, and leave them be without reapplication.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after some days, the joint remains deformed; this causes no harm to the patient as long as the hand is relaxed, and unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries have been cut, so there is nothing else to be tightened except by cauterization near the site, perhaps even nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned earlier, then strain it and leave for five days, then release the strain and leave as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they cannot move it properly, and there is any tear or injury, then apply a compress of warm water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then stretch the finger, and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns to its place, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjoined; leave it for two days, and then put it even that day; at night bind it as we have said, and in the morning unbind it, and make it move, and re-bind it at night; do this frequently until it becomes straight again, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, doing what you did before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, as death quickly takes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the patient involuntarily releases urine, cannot control it, and often has weakness in certain limbs, such as both thighs or both arms or one. And sometimes the spine twists into four parts; this twisting towards the back is called "gilbositez": the cure for this is to reverse it if it came about in childhood: there is no cure nor healing from this condition.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes about due to falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure were longwinded, and not very beneficial; but I have made them shorter according to my understanding, and have fashioned instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hunchback condition affecting the lower back, no one is aware of it beforehand; and likewise for those directly affected on both sides, you cannot treat with force unless it comes to the back, as I have said; so that the patient should be stretched out face down onto an even surface without bruising themselves, then fix a poker into the ground at the head firmly and another between the feet, bind a rope over the hips of the patient, and another around the waist, knees, and ankles; two assistants should hold these ropes, one by the head, and the other by the feet, in line with each of the pokers; and let them be well secured, as we have said for the pokers, and let the healer place their palms on the spine firmly until it regains its shape.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arm lengths long, and fix it under the wall, and let the patient be on their side, then push the head of the board underneath the wall, next place the middle of the board onto the spine; have the physicians put their feet on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; if you wish, do it with the turner's tool that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Insert two posts at the patient's head, one arm length apart, and place two more towards their feet with the same distance between them; leave a palm-length space in between each post from top to bottom; make a hole in each post for the turner's tool to fit through, and ensure the posts are firmly embedded into the ground so they do not move; between each pair of these posts, insert another single turning post, upon which the ropes will be wound; this turning post should have two small posts attached that are one palm-length long in order to wind the turner's tool around them; then tie one rope from the turning post by the patient's head and attach it at the other end to the second turning post near their feet, while another rope is tied on the opposite side of each respective turning post so they meet in the middle; have each minister rotate his own turner as far as the rope will allow them to and the master should adjust the spine accordingly as we mentioned before.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is equal, apply a drying poultice with plenty of egg, then the pads, and an iron rod three palms long to clean the place of curvature and the part of the spine which is healthy, then tie it up as we said above, and let the patient feed on subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything happens at the end of healing, one must administer softening and soothing medicines with a handle that I mentioned before, and sometimes a piece of lead is administered or something similar appears behind the vertebra in the back, and they think it is dislocation but this comes from an emergence of bone so there should be no presumption: perhaps it will bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Hip Dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its dislocation is as follows: when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee appears more prominent than the healthy one; the patient cannot bend their knee fully to the ground; and there is an inflamed hot abscess nearby, due to which the head of the thighbone has come loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes naturally is as follows: these accidents are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens in advance is as follows: he stretches his leg well according to its length; however, he cannot bend his knee without pain and if one makes him walk, he cannot go forward but only backward, retains his urine, swells up with anger, and when he defecates, he sits on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has dislocated behind them are such that they cannot straighten their knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, with a softened groin, and the head of the femur is in place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	We treat this type of dislocation by resetting it if the dislocation is old and has remained in its displaced position, following its natural shape, with no treatment needed; there should be no presumption on our part.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one with a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, hasten to reposition the joint, stretching it both inside and outside, and moving it right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and they should firmly hold the leg with two hands, or use a strap tied above the knee; another assistant places their hand under his armpits, then tightly binds his thigh with a rope; another holds the head of the rope; all extend upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground together, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has been corrected, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must treat it in the same way when dislocations are inward, you should lay the patient on their healthy side, then place the strap at the root of the thigh and below the hip joint, then extend the strap upwards towards the hip joint and inguinal ligament; another assistant takes his arms and embraces the thick part of the affected thigh, stretching it outwards strongly: this will return it to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage above the heels and around the knees; let the diseased leg be extended twice as much as the other one; then suspend him from the head of a pole so that he is hanging about two arms' length above the ground. Then instruct your assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, while another attendant hangs with the patient and firmly embraces his thigh because now the joint returns hurriedly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is on the outside, let the patient lie as we have said before in the case of one with curvature (gilbositeit), bind the bandage tightly around the diseased leg and also above the feet; then place two rods, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a rod between the thighs of the patient into the gap; have moistened cloths planted all around so that it does not hurt the patient, then stretch each minister towards him, and let the surgeon put his hand in an equal position to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a flat surface, i.e., a table, and press it as we have described for the treatment of clubfoot, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And for anterior dislocations, you must extend the affected leg gently according to what I've said earlier; place your weight on top of their injured limb and press with the other hand, extending it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.
